- **Saturday:** the wildcard. If she is in-cycle with Storm, Saturday is the day she will most plausibly spend hours in his company. If she is out-of-cycle, Saturday is the day with the highest probability of long-range solitary movement — train trips to towns where she knows no one, museum visits (she is unusually drawn to portraiture, which surveillance interprets without difficulty), and on at least four recorded occasions trips to the vicinity of Alicia Masters's known whereabouts that she did not complete, turning back at some distance.
- **Sunday:** withdrawal day. Minimal outside contact. Extended journal time. The bath is longer. Sleep onset is earlier. The week resets.

---

## 6.10 The Invariants (Diagnostic Markers for Field Identification)

When she is in any shape, the following behaviors persist and are the surveillance team's identification toolkit. They are listed in order of reliability.

1. **Pre-movement hold on waking** (the 90–120 second motionless interval). She does not know she does this and cannot suppress it.
2. **The sternum-then-throat self-check.** Often executed within thirty seconds of any startle, any mirror, any photograph being taken.
3. **The three-count nasal exhale** before any significant action or statement. So embedded it appears mid-combat.
4. **Counter-surveillance turn every three to four blocks while walking.** Independent of cover, location, threat level.
5. **Seat selection facing the entrance.** Universal.
6. **The tip pattern.** She tips a specific percentage (high, consistent) regardless of cover identity. A waiter who has served her in two forms would recognize the same tipper.
7. **The reading-while-eating.** She does not eat in public without something to read, and she does not read on a device in that context.
8. **Aversion behavior at impersonation-plot fiction.** Will exit theaters. Will turn off shows. Will close books.
9. **The candle.** No matter the residence, no matter the form, the evening meal at home is candle-lit. There is always a candle. Surveillance teams have begun to use the candle stock in a residence as a residency-confirmation marker.
10. **The compose-and-delete behavior.** Daily, observable, and the closest thing in the file to a barometer of her interior weather.

---

## 6.11 Summary Characterization

A week in this subject's life is the week of a person engaged in the continuous, exhausting, unwitnessed labor of constructing a self out of the residue of the selves she has been required to inhabit. The routines are not ornamental; they are scaffolding. The candle, the journal, the morning window, the held shape under exertion, the bath — these are not habits in the casual sense. They are the load-bearing infrastructure of an identity that has no native ground to stand on and is being built, hour by hour, day by day, on the only foundation she has found that holds: *the same things, done at the same times, by whoever I am being today.*

A surveillance team watching her for a year would conclude she is one of the most disciplined subjects in the active file. A clinician reading the same data would conclude that the discipline is the symptom — that nothing about a life this ritualized is incidental, and that the woman performing these rituals is, every morning at the window with her coffee too hot, asking the street whether she is allowed to exist today.

The street has not yet answered. She keeps making the coffee.

— UATU, Analytical Stage, section closes.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP: SUBJECT DESIGNATE "LYJA"
## Section 6 — Relationships I: Family & Origin Bonds

---

### Preface to the Section

The conventional category "family of origin" is, in this subject's case, almost entirely a void backfilled by simulation. Lyja's biographical record contains no named biological mother, no named biological father, no confirmed siblings, no Skrull spouse-of-record predating the infiltration mission, and no confirmed living offspring. What exists instead is a *structural* family — the persons and institutions that performed the developmental functions a family of origin ordinarily performs — and the *appropriated* family, the human household she lived inside as Alicia Masters and which became, against operational design, the only kin system she has ever actually metabolized.

This section therefore maps both: the genuine origin bonds we can reconstruct by inference from her training, conditioning, and species-cultural matrix; and the bonds-by-impersonation that functionally substituted for parents, in-laws, and grandparent-figures during the formative adult decade in which her selfhood crystallized around the Alicia template. The two are kept analytically distinct because Lyja cannot keep them distinct herself, and the file's utility depends on doing for her what she cannot do for herself.

A note on absences: the gaps in this section are themselves data. A subject with no parental name available, no sibling network, no aunt/uncle/cousin record, and no homeworld town of provenance — and who has *never on record volunteered any of these details even to intimates* — is a subject who either does not possess such a record consciously, has had it eclipsed by conditioning, or has consciously suppressed it as a security hygiene measure that long ago became character. All three are likely operative.

---

### 6.1 — The Biological Mother (Unnamed, Presumed Skrull Throneworld or Satellite Colony)

No name, no image, no funeral, no anniversary. In ten thousand pages of behavioral observation across forty real-time years, the subject has invoked a mother *zero* times. This is not normal even for trained operatives; even hardened intelligence assets eventually leak a mother-reference under duress, in delirium, in late-stage intimacy. Lyja has not.

Three reading-hypotheses, in descending probability:

**(a)** Mother died or was separated from the subject early enough that no encoded relational template formed — likely during one of the chronic Skrull civil-conflict periods or a Kree border incident. This would account for the apparent ease with which the Skrull state assumed total developmental custody.

**(b)** Mother survives but the bond was severed at the point of operative-selection, an event Lyja appears to have undergone in mid-to-late adolescence given her competence ceiling and the depth of indoctrination required for the Masters mission. The severance would have been framed as honor.

**(c)** Mother was herself a state functionary and the relationship was, from origin, a professional-developmental one rather than a maternal one. Several behavioral signatures support this: the subject's instinctive performance of "mother" while impersonating Alicia (with the Richards children, with Franklin specifically) is curiously imitative rather than instinctive — warm and competent but algorithmic, as if she had studied the form rather than recalled it.

**Trust/Safety:** Not applicable. The bond is a structural absence rather than a relationship with a valence.

**Failure mode the absence produces:** Lyja has no internal "good mother" object to which she can regress in collapse. When destabilized she does not curl inward toward a remembered safe figure; she externalizes toward the current attachment object (Johnny), which is one structural reason that object cannot bear the weight she places on it. The mother-hole is being asked to be filled by a brother-in-law she married, which is not survivable as a long-term arrangement.

**Leverage:** Almost none directly. However, *the imputation of motherhood* to the subject herself is the single most exploitable affective channel in her psychology (see §6.5 on the fabricated child). The absence of a mothered self predisposes her to convert any maternal invitation — real or counterfeit — into an identity-stabilizer. This is precisely how the egg-ruse weaponization worked, against Johnny and, more importantly, against herself.

---

### 6.2 — The Biological Father (Unnamed)

Equally absent from the record, but absent in a different texture. Where the maternal void reads as a *missing template*, the paternal void reads as a *replaced* template: the Skrull state, the Skrull military hierarchy, and specifically the handler-figures who ran her training have collectively occupied the paternal slot. The behavioral evidence is the subject's relationship to authority: she does not rebel against it, she does not idealize it, she *negotiates* with it the way an adult child of a transactional father negotiates — providing competence in exchange for status, withholding affect, never asking for approval she will not receive.

Paibok the Power-Skrull is informative here as a probable proxy for whatever paternal-fraternal figure shaped her in training. The intensity of his lethal response to her divided loyalty — his *personal* fury at her, beyond mission discipline — and her own complete absence of grief at killing or being killed by him, suggest a relationship structured on dominance/contempt rather than care. If Paibok is the closest the file has to an origin-male, the origin-male profile is a violent disciplinarian who experienced her ambivalence as personal betrayal. That is information.

**Trust/Safety:** Inverted. The paternal slot is filled by the institution that would kill her — and did try — for failing to perform. There is no safety here; there is only the avoidance of punishment via competent execution.

**Failure mode:** Lyja over-functions under male authority that frames her as an instrument. She did this for the Skrull command; she did it briefly for Devos; she has at moments slipped into doing it for Reed Richards as institutional patriarch of the FF circle. The reflex is to *earn standing through usefulness*, which is the same reflex that made her marriageable to Johnny inside the cover and which now keeps her circling the team in ally-roles she does not need.

**Leverage:** Authority-framed instructions delivered with neither warmth nor hostility — the cold professional register — produce in her the deepest compliance. Conversely, a paternal-warmth approach is *destabilizing* because she has no template for receiving it and will read it as either manipulation or weakness.

---

### 6.3 — Siblings (None on Record; Implied Cohort)

No biological siblings have ever appeared. What functioned as a sibling cohort, near-certainly, was her training class — the cohort of infiltration operatives selected and processed alongside her. Skrull intelligence-warfare doctrine as observable across the canon (the Super-Skrull program, the Secret Invasion sleeper network, the Paibok cohort) consistently uses small-group conditioning. She would have had peers.

Where are they? Three possibilities, all dark: dead in other operations, still embedded under cover elsewhere, or absorbed into the *Secret Invasion* sleeper network and therefore either killed during the rollback or interned afterward. None of them have ever surfaced in connection to her. She has never sought any of them out, never named one, never reminisced.

This is the single most surveillance-relevant fact in this entire section. **A trained operative who does not reach out to surviving cohort-peers after exposure is either (a) certain they would kill her, (b) certain they are all dead, or (c) certain that any contact would compromise both parties.** All three are plausible; the behavior is identical under any of them. What we can say with confidence is that she has no living sibling-functional contact and does not behave as if she expects to acquire one.

**Failure mode of the missing sibling-system:** Lyja has no horizontal peer-bond in her life. Every relationship she sustains is vertical (above her: the FF as institution, Reed as patriarch; below her: her own protective stance toward Johnny, toward Alicia-in-absentia). She has no equal. This is part of why she cannot integrate — integration is normally witnessed and ratified by peers, and she has none.

**Leverage:** The introduction of a credible peer — another defected Skrull operative, ideally female, ideally from a comparable mission profile — would either be the most stabilizing intervention possible for her or the most catastrophic, depending on whether the peer turned out to be hostile. The asymmetry makes this lever high-value and high-risk; not recommended for casual handler use.

---

### 6.4 — Paibok the Power-Skrull (Functional Sibling/Rival/Executioner)

The closest thing to a named family-of-origin figure in her file, and the relationship is fratricidal. Paibok operated as her partner-handler during the Masters infiltration's terminal phase, presented himself as her intended Skrull mate, and executed her — by his own hand, with apparent personal satisfaction — when her divided loyalty was confirmed (*FF* #358).

The relational dynamic, reconstructed: Paibok regarded Lyja as *his* — his peer, his promised partner, his fellow-augment (he too was bio-engineered for enhanced capacity). Her drift toward authentic feeling for the Storm/Grimm circle was, in his frame, infidelity to him personally before it was treason to the Empire. His attack on her carries the affective signature of a jilted lover, not a disciplinary officer.

For her part, Lyja has never expressed grief over Paibok, never sought reconciliation with him in his subsequent appearances, and has fought him without hesitation. The absence of grief is itself significant: it means either she never reciprocated his framing, or she reciprocated it once and has thoroughly disavowed that part of herself along with the rest of her Skrull-loyalist identity. The behavioral evidence favors the second reading. There is a small but persistent flinch in her recorded interactions with Paibok that is not present with generic Skrull opponents — a familiarity-tell.

**Trust/Safety:** Zero, and the zero is *earned* by attempted murder. This is the cleanest valence in her relational field — the one bond that has resolved into unambiguous enmity.

**Failure mode:** The Paibok bond is the template through which she now reads all Skrull approaches. Any Skrull who attempts to reclaim her she will pre-assimilate to the Paibok schema and refuse on that ground. This is operationally useful (she cannot be re-recruited) but emotionally costly (it forecloses the possibility of any reconciled Skrull identity).

**Leverage:** Threats *from* Paibok produce focused, competent counter-aggression — she is at her most lethal and most coherent against him. Threats *via* Paibok (e.g., framing a third party as Paibok-aligned) work, but only once per handler; she catches the pattern fast.

---

### 6.5 — The Child Who Was Not (Fabricated Offspring, *FF* #383 ff.)

The most psychologically loaded entry in the entire family-section, and the entity has no biological existence. The "egg" presented to Johnny Storm as their child was a Skrull deception — a weaponized fiction Lyja deployed (or allowed to be deployed; the agency-attribution remains slightly murky in canon) to force re-engagement after Johnny's grief-rejection following her exposure.

What matters for this dossier is not the tactical history but the *psychic reality* the deception produced inside the subject. Whether or not there was ever a gestating organism, *Lyja experienced herself as someone who told the father of her child that the child existed and then watched the child be revealed as a lie she had told*. The internal object — the fantasied baby, the imagined parenthood, the projected future — was real to her in the only sense that matters for psychological structure. She mourned an entity she had invented to manipulate, and the mourning was not invented.

This is the entry under which the file logs her single most exploitable and most dangerous affective channel. The fabricated child operates inside her as: 

- a real grief (the loss of an imagined parenthood she briefly inhabited), 
- a real guilt (toward Johnny, for the cruelty of the lie), 
- a real wound to her self-concept (she discovered she was capable of that), and 
- a real reproductive frustration (no actual offspring has ever followed, with anyone).

**Trust/Safety:** Not applicable to the non-entity; but the *memory* of the non-entity is the lowest-safety region of her interior. She will not discuss it. She will leave the room.

**Failure mode:** Any reactivation of the reproductive/parental theme risks repeating the original episode in altered form. She has demonstrated once that the prospect of a child can override her ethical functioning under attachment-threat conditions; she has not been tested on this since, and untested is not the same as healed.

**Leverage:** Severe and prohibited for casual use. The file records this as a *handle-with-extreme-care* lever: effective beyond any other in producing affective collapse, ethically catastrophic to deploy, and likely to produce unpredictable retaliatory behavior afterward. Operational doctrine: do not. Even adversaries who would exploit this lever should be warned that the consequences are not containable.

---

### 6.6 — Alicia Masters (The Person Whose Life She Lived) — Origin-Bond by Theft

Alicia is not Lyja's family by blood, by marriage, or by acquaintance prior to the impersonation — Alicia was, during the infiltration period, in Skrull captivity, *replaced* rather than known. And yet Alicia occupies a structural slot in Lyja's origin-bond field that nothing else can occupy: she is the donor of the only sustained identity Lyja has ever experienced as her own.

This is a kinship of usurpation. Lyja knows Alicia's mannerisms, voice cadence, sculptor's hand-habits, her relationships to her stepfather (the Puppet Master), her gait, her preferences in food and music, the specific quality of her tenderness with Ben Grimm, the particular way she addressed Franklin Richards — and Lyja knows these things not as research but as *embodied memory*, because she performed them for years until they became motor pattern. The Alicia-self is encoded in her musculature, her vocal apparatus, her social reflexes. It cannot be deleted; it can only be foregrounded or suppressed.

The relationship to the actual Alicia, post-recovery, has been almost entirely avoidant on both sides. They have appeared in proximity rarely; they do not converse on record at length; the FF circle has tacitly managed their separation. Alicia has the better moral position — she was the victim — and yet Lyja is the one who carries the harder ongoing burden, because Lyja has to live inside the residue of having *been* Alicia for years. The body remembers what the conscience would prefer to disown.

**Trust/Safety:** Unmeasurable, because untested. Neither woman seeks proximity.

**Failure mode:** The Alicia-self surfaces involuntarily under stress — a phrase, a posture, a turn of phrase Alicia would use, deployed by Lyja without conscious selection. These slippages are the clearest evidence of the dissociative-identity structure logged in §4. The Alicia-self is not a costume in a closet; it is a roommate in the body.

**Leverage:** The single most destabilizing intervention against this subject is to address her *as Alicia* — by name, in Alicia's preferred register, in a context that recalls the Grimm relationship. This has been recorded multiple times in canon producing visible distress disproportionate to the stimulus. The lever is precise, reliable, and ethically grim. Conversely, the most stabilizing intervention is to address her by the name "Lyja" in contexts where the Alicia-self would normally surface — a kind of de-conditioning by repeated naming. No one in her current orbit appears to be doing this systematically.

---

### 6.7 — The Puppet Master (Phillip Masters), by Impersonation-Proxy

During the years Lyja lived as Alicia, she had a stepfather-by-impersonation: Phillip Masters, the Puppet Master, Alicia's actual stepfather and a recurring FF antagonist with complicated familial standing. Lyja's interactions with him during the impersonation period would have required her to perform a daughter-role she had no model for, toward a man whose own affect toward Alicia was a volatile mixture of paternal protection and instrumentalizing manipulation. The role was a difficult one to play; she played it without exposure for years; the strain is undocumented but inferable.

Post-exposure, the relationship has effectively ceased. Masters has shown no interest in her; she has shown none in him. He is, however, *the only living human who once treated her as a daughter*, even if he believed he was treating someone else as a daughter. That fact is filed here because the subject's psychology does not always honor the distinction between bonds-experienced and bonds-authenticated.

**Trust/Safety:** Negligible in either direction. Mutual non-engagement.

**Failure mode:** If Masters were ever to be presented to her in a daughter-framing — a deathbed scene, a custodial appeal — the response would be unpredictable. The role-imprint is there; the activation conditions have not occurred.

**Leverage:** Low-utility, high-uncertainty. Not currently a viable handle.

---

### 6.8 — Franklin Richards and Valeria Richards (Children-by-Impersonation)

During the Alicia years, Lyja was present in Franklin Richards's life as one of his closest adult attachments — Aunt Alicia, the blind sculptor, Uncle Ben's partner, a regular fixture in the Baxter Building home environment. Lyja performed this role through Franklin's earliest formative years. She fed him, comforted him, attended his bedside during nightmares (Skrull infiltration discipline would not permit her to skip these performances), and absorbed his trust completely. Valeria is a more compressed case (born later, post-exposure) but the pattern of affection-by-proximity extends to her in attenuated form.

The relevance to family-of-origin mapping: these children are the closest thing to *children of her own* the subject has ever had in sustained embodied practice. Whatever maternal reflexes she possesses were forged with Franklin in particular. The fabricated-pregnancy episode logged in §6.5 cannot be understood without this context — she knew, at a kinesthetic level, what it was to mother a child, because she had mothered Franklin in fact if not in name.

Post-exposure, Franklin's response to the revelation that "Aunt Alicia" was not Alicia is not extensively documented but appears to have been — characteristically for that child — generous. The relationship has not been re-cultivated by either party. Lyja avoids it; doing so would require explaining herself to a child she once held while he slept.

**Trust/Safety:** Functionally severed but not poisoned. The latent capacity for re-engagement exists; the obstacles are entirely on the adult side.

**Failure mode:** Any harm to Franklin or Valeria would activate in Lyja a protective response *of the same character as harm to her own biological child*. This is not sentimentality on the file's part; it is observable. Her body learned the protect-this-child reflex on these specific children.

**Leverage:** Threats to Franklin or Valeria are operationally exploitable in the same way and at the same intensity as threats to Johnny. Combined threats to all three would produce a complete operational override of every other consideration in her psychology, including self-preservation. This combination is logged as a *do-not-test* condition; the response would be lethal and indiscriminate.

---

### 6.9 — Ben Grimm (Spouse-by-Impersonation; Grief Anchor)

Ben Grimm is the most ethically complicated entry in this entire dossier. He was Alicia's partner. He was also, for nearly a decade of subjective experience, *Lyja's* partner — because she was the one present in the relationship, regardless of which name she answered to. Whatever was real between Alicia and Ben in that period was real-with-Lyja in fact. He held her. He confided in her. He grieved his own monstrousness to her and was comforted. That was Lyja receiving those confidences. Alicia, in captivity, missed all of it.

When the truth surfaced (*FF* #357), the cruelty operated in both directions and the file refuses to rank them. Ben lost a relationship he had believed in; Lyja lost the only intimate-domestic life she had ever inhabited; Alicia lost years of her actual partnership to a substitute who had not asked to want them. Three injured parties, one transgression, distributed unevenly.

Lyja's subsequent management of the Ben-bond is the cleanest evidence in the file that she possesses a functional conscience. She does not approach him. She does not attempt to relitigate. She does not appeal for forgiveness. She accepts that the relationship is owed back to Alicia and absents herself from it. This is mature behavior under guilt-load and should be credited.

What it costs her is also documented: she cannot be around Ben without affective dysregulation. The few panels of post-exposure proximity show her becoming smaller, quieter, and physically oriented away from him — the body-language of someone who has lost a partner she is not permitted to mourn because the mourning itself would be a further insult to the rightful partner.

**Trust/Safety:** A peculiar high-trust/no-contact arrangement. Neither would harm the other. Neither will see the other voluntarily.

**Failure mode:** Ben in mortal danger would draw her out of any cover or commitment she currently holds. She would intervene. She would not stay afterward.

**Leverage:** Threats to Ben work as reliably as threats to Johnny but produce a different action-profile — protective intervention followed by withdrawal, rather than protective intervention followed by approach. Useful distinction for any handler attempting to predict post-incident positioning.

---

### 6.10 — The Skrull Empire (as Family-of-Origin Institution)

The state was her parent. This is not metaphor; it is the structural fact. The Empire selected her, raised her into operative function, augmented her body, deployed her, disowned her when she deviated, and has neither welcomed her back nor permitted her to leave cleanly. Every function ordinarily distributed across a kinship system was concentrated in this one institutional actor.

The post-*Secret Invasion* and *Empyre* developments — the collapse of the old Skrull order, the Kree-Skrull unification under new leadership — present the curious situation in which her parent-institution no longer exists in the form that raised her. The political entity to which she owed and refused loyalty has been succeeded by something else. She has not, on record, sought citizenship or standing in the successor entity. The estrangement from origin-Skrull culture has hardened into estrangement from Skrull-ness generally.

**Trust/Safety:** Adversarial historically; ambiguous currently. The new Skrull-Kree order has not declared her status either way and she has not asked.

**Failure mode:** A formal welcome from the new Skrull leadership would be one of the few interventions capable of producing genuine integration in her — *or* one of the few capable of producing complete decompensation, depending on what conditions accompanied it. The institution's standing offer (or lack thereof) is an unresolved variable in her prognosis.

**Leverage:** Any communication purporting to come from current Skrull authority should be scrutinized; she is not equipped to evaluate the legitimacy of such overtures impartially.

---

### Section Summary

The family-of-origin field for this subject is, in clinical summary: 

- A biological origin so thoroughly suppressed or never-formed that no name, image, or anniversary attaches to any blood relative; 
- An institutional parent (the Skrull state) that filled the developmental slot transactionally and punitively; 
- A single fratricidal quasi-sibling (Paibok) who attempted her execution and forms her template for all Skrull intimates; 
- A fabricated child wh


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

## Preface to the Section

The defining structural fact of Lyja's relational life is that she has **no native social network of her own**. Every name in this section was first encountered through a mission objective, a mistaken identity, or a wound she inflicted. There are no childhood friends in the file. There are no Skrull comrades who survived her defection and still take her calls. There are no neutral parties — no work friends, no neighbors, no clergy, no therapist. The roster below is therefore not a chosen family in the ordinary sense; it is the **set of persons who knew her under one identity and elected, with varying degrees of reluctance, to keep knowing her under another**. The intelligence-relevant pattern is that each of these relationships is structurally **inherited from a deception**, and Lyja's relational behavior with each can be read as a different strategy for metabolizing that original lie.

The roster is short. That itself is the finding.

---

## 1. Johnny Storm — Primary Attachment Object; Estranged Spouse; Recurring Re-Approach Target

### History

The relationship begins in bad faith and never escapes it. Lyja, operating as Alicia Masters, registers Johnny's emotional vulnerability during the period of Ben Grimm's gradual withdrawal — the Secret Wars aftermath, Ben's refusal to return to Earth, the slow vacancy in "Alicia's" home life. She permits, then encourages, then reciprocates Johnny's attention, culminating in the *Fantastic Four* #300 wedding (Englehart, 1986). It is, on the Skrull operational ledger, an *unauthorized escalation*. No mission required her to marry the target's brother-in-arms. She did it. The file's reading is unambiguous: it was the first action she ever took as a person and not as an asset, and she took it without admitting to herself that she was doing so.

The cohabitation period (roughly *FF* #300 through #357) is the longest stretch of stable domestic life she has ever experienced in either identity. It is also the period during which the cover-self most thoroughly colonized the operating-self. By the time of exposure, "loving Johnny" is no longer a performance she is sustaining; it is the only continuous emotional thread her nervous system can locate.

Exposure (*FF* #357–358) ruptures everything at once: marriage, cover, attachment, and species-identity, simultaneously. The egg deception (*FF* #383 and successors) is the post-rupture fallout — a manipulative re-engagement maneuver dressed as a gift of fatherhood, designed to compel proximity, conceived in wounded entitlement and executed with operational competence. Johnny's response — grief, then rage, then a flatter, more durable variant of distrust — sets the terms of every subsequent interaction between them.

From the late DeFalco run through the periodic returns (*Secret Invasion*, the Hickman cameos, *Empyre*, Slott's *FF* vol. 6), the dynamic stabilizes into a recognizable shape: she reappears in his orbit at intervals of months to years, performs a high-risk protective act on his or the team's behalf, accepts no permanent place at the table, and disappears again before the question of *what they actually are to each other* can be asked aloud.

### Dynamics

- **Approach-withdraw oscillation, asymmetric.** Lyja initiates approach; Johnny tolerates it; Lyja initiates withdrawal before he can. The withdrawal is pre-emptive; she leaves so that he will not have to ask her to.
- **Speech pattern in his presence:** measurably slower cadence than her baseline, longer pauses before answering direct questions, a tendency to look at his hands or chest rather than his face. (His face is the face that married Alicia, and looking at it requires her to choose which of them she is in that moment.)
- **Physical proximity protocol:** she will stand within touching distance but does not initiate touch. If he initiates touch, she accepts it with a half-second freeze — observable, brief — and then leans in. The freeze is the dissociative micro-event; the lean is the operating self overriding it.
- **Conflict behavior:** she will not argue with him. Direct accusation produces silence and exit, never defense.

### Evolution

The relationship has shifted from *romantic-deceptive* (pre-exposure) to *guilty-explosive* (egg ruse era) to *grieving-protective* (mid-Nineties) to *ritualized-distant* (*Secret Invasion* onward). In the most recent appearances she behaves toward him with the careful, slightly formal warmth of a war widow toward her dead husband's brother — affection that has accepted it will never again be domestic. He, for his part, has gradually replaced suspicion with a tired, half-fond resignation. Neither has remarried in any way that closes the door.

### Trust / Safety

She trusts him with her life unconditionally. She does not trust him with her *self-account* — she will not tell him what she actually thinks she is. He, conversely, trusts her in a firefight without reservation and does not trust her with any plan that requires her to remain in one place for longer than the mission. This is a stable equilibrium and both parties have, without discussion, agreed to it.

### Failure Mode

The catastrophic failure mode is **engineered indifference from him**. Hostility she can metabolize; grief she can metabolize; even contempt she can metabolize. A demonstration that he has stopped thinking about her at all would collapse the last load-bearing attachment in her psychic architecture and produce, on the historical evidence, either suicidal protective self-sacrifice in his next combat or a regression to the manipulative-reattachment behaviors of the egg-ruse era. The egg ruse is the template; any sufficient abandonment cue can re-trigger it.

### Leverage

Total. Threat to Johnny is the single most reliable predictor of Lyja's behavior in the entire file. An operator who needed her compliance in under thirty seconds would invoke his name; an operator who needed her destroyed would invoke his disinterest.

---

## 2. Ben Grimm — Predecessor Attachment; Permanent Guilt Object; Avoided

### History

Ben is the man she lived with as his fiancée and de facto wife for years while he believed she was Alicia. The relationship was, on Ben's side, the most stabilizing romantic attachment of his adult life. On Lyja's side, it was both the original mission-cover and — by her own intermittent admission — the relationship in which she first learned what tenderness from a man could feel like when it was not performance-coded on his side. The Thing's gentleness toward "Alicia" is a documented anomaly in his behavioral record; it was extended to her without reservation; she received it under false pretenses; and she has never been able to look at him cleanly since.

### Dynamics

- **Avoidance, structural.** She does not seek him out. When circumstance places them in the same room, she positions herself so that another body (usually Johnny's, sometimes Reed's) is between them in her line of sight.
- **Speech to him is shorter than to any other principal in the file** — clipped, factual, transactional. The voice she used as Alicia is the voice she will never use again in his hearing; the absence of it leaves her with nothing fluent to substitute.
- **She has never apologized to him in any extended form on record.** The single closest approach is a brief acknowledgment during the post-exposure arc that what she did to him was the worst thing she has done. He accepted the acknowledgment without absolving it.

### Evolution

The relationship has not evolved. It has petrified. Ben has, over decades, achieved a kind of grim civility toward her — he does not refuse to work with her, does not speak against her to Johnny, does not pursue revenge. He also does not invite her to anything. The actual Alicia Masters' eventual return and resumption of her relationship with Ben closed any door that might have remained; Lyja has, since then, treated Alicia's existence as a fact that requires her to occupy less space.

### Trust / Safety

He trusts her in a fight; he does not trust her in his apartment, his social calendar, or his interior life. She trusts that he will not kill her and does not trust herself to be in a room with him for longer than the mission requires.

### Failure Mode

Sustained proximity to Ben — say, a multi-day mission with no escape — produces in Lyja a cumulative dissociative load that has, in the historical record, manifested as the "Alicia voice" surfacing involuntarily under fatigue. The slippage is brief and she catches it; Ben has caught it too, and the look on his face when he does is, by her own avoidance pattern, the single stimulus she most reliably flees.

### Leverage

Moderate, indirect. She cannot be moved by threat *to* Ben (the guilt is too saturated; another wound to him would not change her behavior, only her grief). She can be moved by **the prospect of being seen by him as having become someone he could respect** — the unsayable wish that drives many of her quiet acts of competence in his theater of operations.

---

## 3. Alicia Masters — The Original; The Returned; The Ghost She Cannot Address

### History

The displaced person. Lyja did not personally abduct Alicia (that was upstream Skrull operations during the *Secret Wars* extraction), but Lyja is the entity whose existence depended on Alicia's absence and whose continued partial-existence as "the woman who was Alicia" depends on Alicia's continued forbearance. When Alicia was recovered and her relationship with Ben restored, Lyja's most foundational cover identity was retroactively converted from *successful imposture* to *stolen life now returned to its owner* — a reclassification she has never recovered from.

### Dynamics

There is essentially no on-record direct dyadic interaction sustained beyond minutes. The two women have been in the same building, the same room, the same crisis; they have not had a conversation. Lyja's pattern in Alicia's presence is to be **operationally elsewhere** — she finds the task that takes her out of the room. Alicia, who is blind, has nonetheless on at least one occasion remarked on Lyja's voice with the steady, unsettling accuracy of a sculptor; the file's reading is that Alicia can hear the residual shape of her own intonations in Lyja's voice and that Lyja knows this and cannot bear it.

### Trust / Safety

Not applicable in operational terms. The relevant metric is **psychic load**. Alicia is the only person in the universe whose mere existence proves Lyja's most coherent self was a theft. There is no relationship to trust or distrust; there is only the unrepayable debt.

### Failure Mode

Direct, sustained interaction would produce — and the avoidance pattern is precisely calibrated to prevent — the question Lyja has spent decades not asking herself: *whose affects were those, then, that I felt for Ben? Mine, or hers, performed through me until they leaked?* The question is unanswerable and asking it would, on the clinical evidence, precipitate a major dissociative episode.

### Leverage

Latent and severe. Any actor who could engineer a forced extended interaction between Lyja and Alicia — particularly one in which Alicia were to extend forgiveness or, worse, kindness — would be wielding the single most psychologically destabilizing instrument available against the subject. Recommend this scenario be flagged and never deliberately constructed; the collateral risk to both women is high.

---

## 4. Reed Richards — Reluctant Sponsor; Distrusted Necessity

### History

Reed is the man who exposed her (*FF* #357–358) and the man who, repeatedly since, has accepted her intelligence offerings, processed her returns, and permitted her presence in Baxter Building space. He has never extended warmth. He has extended **procedural fairness**, which is, from him, a significant allocation.

### Dynamics

- **Interaction is briefing-shaped.** She delivers; he receives; he interrogates for inconsistency; she answers; the meeting ends. Neither party offers personal content.
- **She respects his intelligence and fears his capacity to read her** — accurately the most analytically dangerous person in her social field, because he is the one most likely to model her contradictions back to her with a precision she could not survive hearing.
- **He, for his part, has classified her as a high-utility, high-risk asset and behaves consistently with that classification.** He does not pretend to like her. He does not refuse to work with her. The arrangement is sustainable precisely because it is honest.

### Evolution

Stable across decades. Slight thaw post-*Secret Invasion*, when her intelligence work measurably saved lives; nothing approaching friendship.

### Trust / Safety

She trusts his **judgment** without trusting his **inclination toward her**. He trusts her **information** without trusting her **stability**. Both assessments are accurate.

### Failure Mode

If Reed were ever to render an unsolicited *psychological* assessment of her aloud — to articulate, in his clinical-systems voice, what she is — the resulting destabilization would be severe. He knows this. He has, observably, declined to do so. The forbearance is one of his quieter kindnesses and she knows it is a kindness and resents needing it.

### Leverage

Reed is the *gatekeeper* node. Access to Johnny, to the Baxter Building, to operational legitimacy in human space, runs through Reed's tolerance. Any actor seeking to sever Lyja from her support network would work through Reed, not around him.

---

## 5. Sue Storm — Sister-In-Law-Who-Never-Was; Quiet Adjudicator

### History

Sue was, briefly and across a great deception, Lyja's sister-in-law. Sue welcomed "Alicia" into the family long before the marriage to Johnny — Sue is the family member most invested in extended-family cohesion — and the warmth was real on Sue's side and *received as real* on Lyja's. The exposure was, on the relational ledger, as much a betrayal of Sue's hospitality as of anyone's.

### Dynamics

- Sue's behavior toward Lyja in the years since exposure is the **most behaviorally interesting** in the entire roster. Sue does not forgive easily and does not pretend to. She also does not exile. She has, on multiple occasions, addressed Lyja directly and at moderate length — asked her actual questions about her actual state, the kind of questions no one else in the circle will ask — and listened to the answers without flinching.
- This is the only relationship in Lyja's file in which she is **regularly asked how she is and expected to answer**.
- She finds the experience nearly intolerable and keeps showing up for it.

### Evolution

From maternal warmth (pre-exposure, false) to sharp, almost prosecutorial cold (immediate post-exposure) to a slowly recovered, recalibrated, *adult* engagement in which Sue treats her as a person whose conduct will be evaluated incident by incident. This is the only relational thread in Lyja's life that has demonstrated a forward trajectory rather than a holding pattern.

### Trust / Safety

The highest-bandwidth trust in Lyja's file, paradoxically with the woman who has least reason to extend it. Sue trusts Lyja to **not be lying right now** in a way no one else does, and Lyja, in Sue's presence specifically, exhibits the lowest rate of dissociative speech-slippage in the dataset. The hypothesis: Sue's force-field-derived habit of *holding* difficult things steady extends, unconsciously, to holding Lyja's identity steady for the duration of a conversation.

### Failure Mode

Sue's disappointment is the only sanction in Lyja's social field that operates faster than Johnny's anger. A specific tone Sue uses — the lowered, measured one she reserves for serious failure — has been observed to produce immediate behavioral correction in Lyja within the same scene.

### Leverage

Sue is the **single best route** to communicating with Lyja honestly about her own conduct. Any handler seeking genuine behavioral change rather than tactical compliance would work through Sue. Sue would also detect manipulation of this channel within minutes and end the access; the lever is real but cannot be exploited.

---

## 6. Franklin and Valeria Richards — Children Once Held Under False Pretenses

### History

Lyja, as "Alicia," held Franklin as an infant. She has, in the post-exposure decades, encountered both Richards children at varying ages. Her behavior toward them is the **most regressively tender** in the file and the most carefully restrained.

### Dynamics

- She does not initiate physical contact with either child. Ever.
- She speaks to them with the careful, slightly formal warmth of an aunt who has been told she may visit but not stay.
- Franklin, who perceives more than he says, has shown her a degree of unguarded openness that nearly breaks her composure on record; she manages it by keeping interactions brief.
- Valeria, who perceives everything and says most of it, has on at least one occasion asked her a direct question about her species and her marriage that no adult would have dared; Lyja answered honestly and the encounter is the closest thing to a confessional in her recent file.

### Trust / Safety

The children trust her in the uncomplicated way children trust adults who are visibly careful with them. She trusts herself around them only in the presence of at least one other adult — a self-imposed protocol traceable to the egg-ruse era and her own private terror of what she did with the concept of a child.

### Failure Mode

Any harm to either child while she is present would, on the behavioral evidence, produce a self-destructive intervention exceeding even her response to threats against Johnny. The children occupy the **atonement-target** position in her psychic economy: protecting them is the only available currency in which she can repay what she did with the false pregnancy.

### Leverage

Do not use. The leverage exists and is enormous; any actor invoking it would be invoking a force exceeding their ability to control.

---

## 7. Paibok the Power-Skrull — Former Comrade; Killer; Mirror

*[Treated more fully in Relationships I; included here for cross-reference because his absence shapes the chosen-family roster.]*

The single relevant point for this section: Paibok is the only Skrull who ever knew her well enough to be classified as intimate, and he is the Skrull who killed her for divided loyalty. His existence in her file forecloses the possibility of a Skrull chosen family. **There is no one of her own people she can go home to.** Every name above this entry occupies a slot that, in a healthier life, would have been filled by a fellow Skrull. The roster is short because the alternative roster was murdered out of her access by Paibok's gun.

---

## 8. The Skrull Diaspora (Post-*Secret Invasion*, *Empyre* Era) — Adjacent Community, Not Joined

### History

The post-*Secret Invasion* dispersal and the *Empyre*-era Kree-Skrull unification produced, for the first time in her life, a **population of Skrulls living outside Empire command structures**, many of them themselves former deep-cover assets, many of them carrying analogous dissociative wounds. This is, in principle, the natural community for her. She has not joined it.

### Dynamics

She has had cordial, low-intensity contact with diaspora figures on operational matters. She has declined invitations to participate in the community's collective identity-reconstruction work. The pattern is consistent with her overall refusal to commit to any singular identity-frame.

### Trust / Safety

Wary mutual respect. They know what she did; some of them did analogous things. The shared knowing is precisely what makes proximity intolerable — they would *see her clearly* in a way the human circle cannot, and being seen clearly is the experience she has spent her life avoiding.

### Failure Mode

If pressed by the diaspora to choose — to publicly identify as Skrull, to take a role in their reconstruction — she will withdraw. The withdrawal is itself a data point the diaspora has noted and stopped testing.

### Leverage

Low and unreliable. The diaspora is not invested enough in her to compel her, and she is not invested enough in it to be moved.

---

## 9. Mentors — None on Record

The file contains **no identifiable mentor figure**. Her Skrull trainers are unnamed in canon and were, by the nature of indoctrination training, anti-mentors — they shaped her capacities while preventing the formation of a self that could own them. No human figure has occupied a mentor role; Reed is too distrustful, Sue too peer-positioned, Johnny too entangled, Ben too wounded. 

This absence is structurally significant. **The category of "person who taught me who I am and wished me well in being it" is empty in her life.** Many of the behavioral pathologies catalogued in §3–§4 of the master file would be substantially mitigated by the presence of such a figure; the failure of any such figure to emerge across decades of opportunity is itself diagnostic, and reflects her own active selection against the role. She does not seek mentors. To accept one would require disclosing which self was being mentored.

---

## 10. Proteges — None on Record; One Latent Candidate

No formal mentee. The latent candidate is **Valeria Richards**, whose interest in Lyja as a *subject of inquiry* (species, biology, identity-architecture) has, on at least one occasion, prompted Lyja to answer questions about herself with a candor she extends to no adult. The relationship is not pedagogic and Lyja would refuse the framing, but if any individual in her social field is positioned to one day extract from her a coherent self-account, it is the Richards daughter. The file flags this as a **prospective long-horizon development** rather than a current relationship.

---

## Cross-Cutting Findings

1. **The roster is composed entirely of persons she first knew under a false identity.** There is not a single relationship in her chosen-family field that began with both parties knowing who she was. This is the foundational structural fact of her social existence.
2. **Sue Storm is the most behaviorally productive relationship in her life** and is consistently under-utilized in operational thinking about her. She is treated as Johnny's sister; she is, in fact, Lyja's only adult adjudicator.
3. **The children occupy the atonement slot.** They are not friends; they are the moral center of gravity in her current behavior. Protecting them is how she pays.
4. **The absence of Skrull intimates is total** and produces a one-sided dependency on human attachments that no healthy psychic economy could sustain indefinitely.
5. **The absence of mentors is self-selected** and is one of the principal obstacles to any further integration.

Her chosen family is, in the end, the family she stole from, returned to, and was permitted — by an act of collective forbearance whose generosity she has never fully acknowledged — to remain at the edge of. Every name above is a creditor who has agreed not to call in the debt. She lives on that forbearance and she knows it. It is the closest thing to a home she has.

— UATU, Analytical Stage, section closes.


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP: SUBJECT DESIGNATE "LYJA"
## Section: Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

---

The relational map below is partitioned not by moral category (the subject does not file her own attachments that way) but by functional valence in the subject's intrapsychic economy. Several figures occupy more than one category simultaneously — the defining feature of the Lyja record is that her enemies were her lovers, her lovers were her marks, and her marks became the only people who ever called her by anything resembling a name. The reader should hold that contamination in mind throughout.

---

### I. INTIMATES / LOVERS

#### 1. Jonathan Lowell Spencer "Johnny" Storm — primary attachment object, husband-of-record, central organizing wound

**History.** Initial contact: as "Alicia," during the late-Byrne/early-Englehart period of cohabitation in the Baxter Building, when Ben Grimm's withdrawal into self-pity and the Thing's body-image collapse created a vacuum into which Johnny stepped first as comforter, then suitor. The subject's mission parameters did not require this development. The record is unambiguous: Lyja could have maintained cover indefinitely as Ben's ex without progressing to Johnny. She progressed anyway. The wedding (*FF* #300, 1986) is the operational anomaly that defines the entire file — a Skrull asset stood at an altar, took vows in a borrowed face, and according to the behavioral residue *meant them*.

**Dynamics.** The relationship runs on a triple deception that Johnny detects only in retrospect: the species deception, the identity deception, and — most corrosive — the deception by which Lyja conceals from *herself* that she is no longer performing. With Johnny she is most fully Alicia; with Johnny, after exposure, she becomes most fully nothing. The post-#357 conversations between them (cf. the Devos arc, the Hyperstorm arc, the journey through alternate realities) follow a fixed choreography: he attempts to engage the woman he married; she answers as the woman who deceived him; neither acknowledges that there is a third party in the room — the Lyja who exists only in the relational field between them and has no other site of existence.

**Evolution.** Five discrete phases:
1. *Cover phase (pre-#357):* Skrull operative simulating wife. Affect: warm, controlled, mission-aligned. Sleep patterns regular, body language Alicia-calibrated to a degree that fooled Ben Grimm at intimate range — a feat of impersonation that should be classified as an intelligence-craft milestone in its own right.
2. *Exposure / death-and-return phase (#357–383):* role collapse, capture, reconditioning attempts by Skrull medical, escape, ambivalent re-contact.
3. *Egg deception phase (#383–392):* the dispositive episode. Lyja, having been rejected by Johnny on grounds she could not contest, fabricated a pregnancy and presented him a Skrull egg as their child. The cruelty is calibrated. She knew where to put the knife because she had inventoried his interior for years.
4. *Atonement phase (#393–416):* serial self-endangerment on Johnny's behalf, no requests made, no relationship resumed.
5. *Diasporic / liminal phase (*Secret Invasion* onward):* intermittent contact, no resolution sought or offered, both parties having quietly accepted that the marriage exists in a tense the language does not contain.

**Trust / safety.** Trust asymmetric and inverted. Johnny trusts her *in crisis* absolutely — her record of physical protection is unbroken — and trusts her *intimately* not at all. She trusts him to be the lever others will pull. Safety for her is being near him; safety for him is having her in his peripheral vision rather than in his bed.

**Failure mode.** Abandonment cues from Johnny produce the worst version of the subject. The egg ruse is the prototype, not an outlier. If pushed again to the precise interpersonal coordinates of that episode — public romantic rejection by Johnny, no operational mission to displace into, no Skrull command structure to absorb her — predicted behavior includes manipulative re-engagement via shared symbolic content (the marriage, a fabricated mutual obligation, an invented threat she alone can resolve). She will not harm him. She will harm the version of him that exists inside her in order to force the outer version to look at her.

**Leverage.** For benevolent handlers: a credible, sustained signal that Johnny sees her as *Lyja* — not as the woman who wore Alicia's face, not as his estranged wife, but as the third person — would do more therapeutic work than any intervention available. For malign actors: threaten Johnny and she will arrive within the hour, in any body, under any constraint.

---

#### 2. Benjamin Jacob Grimm — first cover-spouse, present-tense unresolved guilt object

**History.** The subject inhabited Alicia Masters's life beginning approximately *FF* #265–270, displacing the real Alicia (held in Skrull captivity through the duration). For roughly the entire interval of Ben's most psychologically vulnerable years — the Secret Wars return, the *post-*Secret Wars cohabitation in the apartment off Yancy Street, the period of his estrangement from the team — the woman in his bed and at his easel was Lyja. The intimacy was total. Ben, whose body-image pathology made him chronically convinced no woman could love him, was being loved by a woman who was not a woman and not the person he believed her to be, and the love itself, by all behavioral evidence, was at least partially real on her side.

**Dynamics.** Where the Johnny relationship is the loud wound, the Ben relationship is the quiet one. Lyja almost never speaks of Ben on the record after exposure. When his name appears in her vicinity she becomes still in a particular way — the spy's stillness, used here to suppress affect rather than to gather it. She did not love Ben the way she came to love Johnny, but she *knew* Ben more deeply than she knew Johnny, because the impersonation of Alicia required her to study Ben as a continuous object for years.

**Evolution.** Cover-intimacy → operational withdrawal (as the Skrull plan shifted toward Johnny) → off-screen absence during the post-exposure decade → minimal direct contact thereafter. There is no reconciliation arc in the record. There is also no hostility. There is the silence of a debt acknowledged and known to be unpayable.

**Trust / safety.** Ben does not trust her and does not need to; their relational vector no longer crosses an intimate plane. He has, in canon, declined opportunities to denounce her, which the subject's file should register as a kindness she has not earned and cannot reciprocate. Safety: high in both directions, because distance is maintained.

**Failure mode.** Forced proximity to Ben — a hostage scenario, a forced team-up — would produce regression to over-performance of competence and avoidance of eye contact. She would not decompensate operationally. She would decompensate hours later, alone.

**Leverage.** Invoking the name "Alicia" in her presence destabilizes her more than any direct threat. The reason is Ben, not Alicia herself. Alicia is the stolen identity; Ben is the man she stole it *from*. This is the dosage point of greatest vulnerability in the entire file.

---

#### 3. Paibok — Skrull peer, would-be mate, executioner, recurring antagonist

**History.** Paibok the Power-Skrull was Lyja's contemporary and presumed intended partner within Skrull operational culture — the closest figure in her record to a same-culture intimate. The exact pre-mission relationship is sparsely documented; the inferential picture is of a betrothal or quasi-betrothal disrupted by Lyja's deep-cover assignment, with Paibok cultivating the grievance during her absence. On her exposure (*FF* #357–358) Paibok did not attempt recovery or extraction. He killed her.

**Dynamics.** This is the only relationship in the file in which the subject is the betrayed party rather than the betrayer. Its psychological function is therefore enormous: it preserves a thin warrant for her self-conception as a person who can be wronged, who has a side to be on, and against whom violence has been done. She is unable to relinquish him as antagonist because doing so would erase the one frame in which she is morally legible to herself.

**Evolution.** Pre-mission ambiguous-intimate → executioner → recurring enemy across the Dreadface and subsequent arcs → late-stage rare appearances where the hatred is ritualized rather than active. She has not killed him in canon and has had opportunities. The file should note this. He has not finished killing her either.

**Trust / safety.** Zero trust, calibrated threat awareness. Paradoxically, this is one of her *safer* relationships in the psychological sense — the parameters are clear, no identity confusion is in play, she knows exactly what she is to him and he to her.

**Failure mode.** If Paibok were to claim, credibly, that he had loved her — that the killing had been jealousy rather than judgment — she would not be able to process it cleanly. He has not yet made this move. If he ever does, predict destabilization.

**Leverage.** None usable. He is the closest thing in her life to a fixed star.

---

### II. RIVALS

#### 4. Alicia Masters — the displaced original; ontological rival; non-combatant

**History.** Alicia Masters is the woman whose life Lyja consumed for the better part of a decade. After Alicia's recovery and return (post-#357), the two women have shared remarkably little on-page interaction, which itself is data: the avoidance is mutual and load-bearing.

**Dynamics.** Alicia is not Lyja's enemy. Alicia is something worse — Alicia is the proof that there was always a real one, and that everything tender Ben Grimm ever said to "his wife" was being said *past* Lyja to a woman in a Skrull holding cell. Every memory the subject has of being loved is contaminated by the existence of the person the love was actually addressed to. There is no resolution to this and there cannot be one.

**Evolution.** Unwitting victim → restored citizen → permanent ambient presence in the FF circle whom Lyja systematically does not occupy a room with. Across the entire post-exposure record there is, to this analyst's reading, no scene of substantive reconciliation between them. The avoidance is a treaty.

**Trust / safety.** Alicia poses no operational threat. The threat is ontological. Safety is maintained through Lyja's strict avoidance of Alicia's sensory and social proximity.

**Failure mode.** A forced encounter in which Alicia speaks to her kindly would produce one of two outcomes: collapse into apology she has rehearsed and cannot deliver, or flight. Alicia's documented temperament makes the kindness scenario the more probable, which makes the rivalry, paradoxically, more dangerous than if Alicia hated her.

**Leverage.** Alicia is a passive lever. A handler need not move her; her existence is the lever. Mentioning her well-being suffices.

---

#### 5. Susan Storm Richards — sister-in-law-of-record; the unblinking observer

**History.** Sue knew "Alicia" intimately through the cover years — confidante, eventually sister-in-law via the Johnny marriage. Post-exposure Sue's posture is unique in the FF and warrants close reading: she is the team member who neither forgives reflexively (Johnny's pattern) nor avoids (Ben's pattern) nor declares enmity (no one's pattern). She watches.

**Dynamics.** Sue is the only person in the subject's relational field whose threat-assessment of Lyja is approximately accurate. Sue grasps that Lyja's loyalty is real and that her judgment under abandonment stress is not to be trusted. She has, in canonical reading, extended Lyja conditional trust under operational duress and has withheld it socially. This is correct policy and Lyja knows it is correct, which is one of the few stable points in her current self-model.

**Evolution.** Trusted intimate-by-proxy → exposed deceiver → conditionally tolerated ally. The vector is glacial; Sue does not rush these.

**Trust / safety.** Lyja trusts Sue to be fair. Sue trusts Lyja to perform. Neither trusts the other socially. Both are correct.

**Failure mode.** If Sue ever explicitly classified her as family — a maternal gesture rather than a tactical one — Lyja would not be able to absorb it. She would not retaliate. She would disappear for a period of months.

**Leverage.** Sue's good opinion is one of the few currencies the subject still pursues. Sue's *withdrawal* of regard is a more potent disciplinary tool against Lyja than any restraint Reed could engineer.

---

#### 6. Crystalia Amaquelin (Crystal) — historical romantic rival, vestigial

**History.** Johnny Storm's prior significant attachment, periodically reactivated in his interior weather. During Lyja's cover years and afterward, Crystal functioned in the subject's mental landscape as the baseline against which Lyja measured her grip on Johnny.

**Dynamics.** Largely intrapsychic; the two women do not extensively engage on-page. The rivalry is one-sided in the sense that Crystal does not appear to register it, and Lyja, with her trained social intelligence, knows Crystal does not register it, which sharpens rather than dulls the resentment.

**Evolution.** From operational anxiety (a Skrull asset assessing competitors for the cover spouse's affection) to personal anxiety (a wife assessing competitors for her husband's heart) — a transition the subject did not notice when it occurred. Post-exposure, the rivalry has gone dormant but is reliably reactivated by any narrative reminder of Johnny's pre-marriage life.

**Failure mode.** None acute. A slow corrosive comparison the subject runs against herself in private.

**Leverage.** Low. Useful only as a destabilizer in combination with abandonment cues.

---

### III. ENEMIES

#### 7. The Skrull Empire (institutional) — abandoning parent, hunting state

**History.** Recruiter, trainer, augmenter, deployer, and — on exposure of her divided loyalty — would-be executioner of the subject. The relationship is best modeled as a parental one in an abusive register: total formative authority, conditional acceptance, violent withdrawal of recognition on noncompliance.

**Dynamics.** The Empire's claim on her is the only thing that ever told her who she was. Losing that claim did not free her; it unhoused her. Her behavior toward Skrull operations after exposure is over-determined: she opposes them, but with a precision and grief that betrays continued investment in their not being what they have become.

**Evolution.** Authority → betrayer-of-self → enemy → during *Secret Invasion*, exposed as enemy to the Empire's most expansionist faction → in the *Empyre* reframing under the new Skrull-Kree synthesis, a more complicated set of claims reopens, none of which she has accepted.

**Trust / safety.** No trust, sustained threat awareness. She is on a Skrull kill list of indeterminate priority and has been for decades.

**Failure mode.** An offer of *re-acceptance* by a credible Skrull authority — return-without-punishment, restoration of standing — would be the single most psychologically dangerous offer ever placed before her, more so than any threat. She might refuse. She would not refuse cleanly.

**Leverage.** A handler who could credibly broker even partial restoration of Skrull civil standing for her would acquire a degree of influence over the subject's behavior that would border on coercive.

---

#### 8. Devos the Devastator — operational antagonist of the early defection period

**History.** Adversary during the arc in which Lyja's defection was operationalized in field combat alongside the FF (*FF* circa #375 onward). Devos served as the proving-ground enemy against whom Lyja could demonstrate, to the team and to herself, that the new loyalty was real.

**Dynamics.** Functionally a *useful* enemy — the kind a destabilized subject needs in order to externalize identity conflict into combat. Lyja's performance against Devos was crisp, eager, and slightly over-extended in ways suggesting she was using the engagement as therapy.

**Failure mode.** None specific.

**Leverage.** Low. Devos is significant in the file only as evidence that the subject can metabolize identity confusion into competent violence against a discrete external target.

---

#### 9. Dreadface — possession-class threat, vector of role-confusion

**History.** The Dreadface entity, encountered during the same arc, possessed members of the FF and represented a categorically distinct threat: a being whose entire modality was the involuntary occupation of another's identity. The thematic resonance for the subject is obvious and was likely not lost on her.

**Dynamics.** Lyja's engagement with the Dreadface arc carries an audible note of personal disgust beyond mission requirements. She was fighting, in effigy, what had been done to her — and what she had done to others.

**Failure mode.** Possession-class threats specifically should be expected to produce disproportionate response from this subject, including risk-acceptance well beyond mission parameters.

**Leverage.** None offensive. Operationally, deploy her against identity-violation threats by preference; she will outperform baseline.

---

#### 10. Hyperstorm — existential / lineage threat

**History.** The Hyperstorm arc placed Lyja in proximity to a Richards-line existential antagonist during a period in which her own claim on family-of-record (Johnny, the child-that-was-not) was actively collapsing. Her performance in the arc included sustained self-endangerment on Johnny's behalf.

**Dynamics.** Hyperstorm functions in the file as the enemy against whom the subject definitively re-earned her right to remain in the FF's orbit, at the cost — possibly the intended cost, from her unconscious's vantage — of nearly dying again.

**Failure mode.** She will accept lethal risk in any scenario framed as protection of the Storm-Richards lineage. This is not heroism in the ordinary sense; it is structured atonement, and like all atonement behaviors in this subject it is unbounded.

**Leverage.** A scenario framed around lineage-threat will produce maximum compliance and maximum risk-acceptance.

---

#### 11. The Super-Skrull (Kl'rt) — ambivalent elder, neither lover nor enemy in the simple sense

**History.** Kl'rt's relationship to the subject is intermittent and largely institutional through most of her career — a senior Skrull whose loyalties have themselves been famously unstable. In the post-*Secret Invasion* and *Empyre* periods, his diasporic trajectory parallels hers more than either would admit.

**Dynamics.** He is one of the very few Skrulls who can stand in a room with her without the encounter resolving into combat or recruitment attempt. The relationship reads as that of two estranged veterans of the same lost regiment, neither willing to debrief.

**Failure mode.** None active. Watch for slow drift: if the file shows increasing voluntary co-location with Kl'rt over a sustained period, infer that the subject is beginning to construct a Skrull-side adult community for herself, which would represent the first genuine integration movement in the record.

**Leverage.** Kl'rt's regard, if cultivated, would constitute a second anchor beside the Storm orbit — strategically the single most stabilizing development imaginable for the subject's prognosis (cf. §3, §5 of the master workup). A handler interested in her long-term integration should consider Kl'rt-proximate operations a priority.

---

### IV. CROSS-CUTTING OBSERVATION

The reader will note that the subject's intimates and enemies overlap heavily — Paibok was nearly both; the Empire was parent and executioner; Johnny is husband, victim, lever, and unfinished sentence; Alicia is non-combatant rival whose existence indicts every tender memory. This is not a coincidence of plotting. It is the relational signature of a subject whose original training required her to *be* her targets, and who consequently cannot maintain the categorical distinction — lover / rival / enemy — that ordinarily organizes a human life. Her file resists this section's own headings. That resistance is itself the finding.

— UATU, Analytical Stage, Relationships III closes.


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP: SUBJECT DESIGNATE "LYJA"
## Section 6 — Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

---

### 6.1 The Cellular Substrate: Skrull Plasticity, Baseline

The subject's primary capability is the Deviant-Skrull morphological plasticity common to her species: voluntary, cellularly-mediated reorganization of body form, mass distribution, pigmentation, dermal texture, voice apparatus, and (within tolerances discussed below) apparent biological function. The mechanism, as canon presents it and as the file reconstructs it, is not "illusion" in the optical sense — she is not projecting an image while remaining covertly green-and-corrugated underneath. The transformation is somatic. A pathologist taking a tissue sample from "Alicia Masters" during the *Fantastic Four* #265–356 window would have found human-presenting tissue down to the level any non-specialist could verify. This matters operationally: she defeats casual medical examination, defeats touch, defeats intimate cohabitation, defeats — crucially — Ben Grimm's tactile sense and Johnny Storm's prolonged proximity in shared domestic and sexual life. The deception is not a layer; it is the body.

**Range of morphology.** Within observed canon she has assumed: a single, sustained, complete adult human female impersonation (Alicia) maintained for years of in-story continuity without observable slip; a fully restored "native" Lyja form (the green-skinned, ridge-jawed Skrull baseline); a hybridized presentation she has used in later appearances — humanoid with subtle Skrullness retained (pointed ears, slight pigment shift) which reads as her *chosen* face, neither full disguise nor full native form; and tactical morph-adjustments mid-combat (mass shifts, limb elongation, brief mimicry of opponents). She has not been documented attempting non-humanoid forms (animals, objects, the Super-Skrull stunt of becoming a chair), which may indicate either training emphasis (she is an infiltrator, not a shock-troop morpher) or genuine ceiling.

**Mass conservation.** Skrull morphology generally observes approximate mass conservation; Lyja conforms. She cannot become a child convincingly without storing the displaced mass somewhere, and there is no evidence she has solved that problem the way some Skrull operatives have. This implicitly defines the impersonation pool available to her at any given moment: adult humanoids of roughly her own mass range. Alicia Masters was a close match. This is unlikely to be coincidence — Skrull mission planning would have selected her *because* the target body and her own were biometrically compatible.

**Duration.** This is the file's most under-appreciated datum. The Alicia impersonation was held for *years* of continuous waking life — through sleep, through sex, through illness, through unconscious moments after physical trauma. This implies that her assumed form is not a held muscular act but a re-stabilized resting state. She can sleep as Alicia. She can be knocked unconscious as Alicia and not revert. Comparative evidence from other Skrulls suggests this level of stability requires either deep training, deep psychological investment in the role, or both. In her case: both, and the latter became the problem (see §3, §4, and §6.7 below).

---

### 6.2 The Retrofitted Weapon System: Flare-Blasts

Lyja's secondary capability is bio-engineered rather than native: the projection of concussive/incendiary energy "flares" from the hands, introduced in the post-*FF* #358 reconditioning arc when Skrull medical authority rebuilt her after Paibok's attack and weaponized the asset they had recovered. The mechanism is not specified in canon beyond visual coding (orange-yellow plasma-like discharge, not the cold "stellar" green of Skrull tech) and a clear association with her hands as emitters.

**Behavioral inference about the mechanism:** The flares appear metabolically costly. She does not spam them; she uses them in punctuated bursts, then reverts to shapeshift-and-evade tactics. There is no on-record demonstration of sustained beam-fire, area-effect detonation, or scaling to Human-Torch-comparable output. Working estimate: low-to-mid superhuman energy projection, sufficient to stagger a Skrull combatant or breach a wall, insufficient to threaten a top-tier metahuman head-on.

**Targeting and control:** Precise. She has used flares to disable equipment, sever restraints, and produce non-lethal incapacitation when her objective was capture-or-warning rather than kill. This contrasts revealingly with Paibok's blunt-instrument application of his own augmented arsenal — she fights like a spy who was given a gun, not like a soldier who was issued one.

**Symbolic reading:** Marvel's iconography is rarely innocent. Lyja was given fire by the people who built her, in the same period she was being rebuilt to re-pursue the man who already *was* fire. The Skrull engineers either made a darkly literal joke or unconsciously equipped her to compete with the rival they could not eliminate. She has never, on record, used the flares against Johnny — though she has used them in his defense. The weapon her old masters gave her, she has redirected entirely toward their enemies and her own.

---

### 6.3 Tradecraft: The Invisible Power Set

The shapeshifting and the flares are the visible powers. The dispositive capability is tradecraft. The Alicia operation is, on its merits, one of the most successful long-duration human-impersonation infiltrations in the recorded Marvel canon — sustained against a target group containing a telepath-adjacent intellect (Reed Richards), a tactile genius (Ben Grimm, who shared her bed), an investigative socialite (Sue), and an unstable empath (Johnny). She passed all of them, for years, without triggering suspicion sufficient to act on. This requires:

- **Linguistic and idiomatic mastery** of contemporary American English at native fluency, including the specific dialectal register of a young woman raised in Lower East Side artistic circles by the Puppet Master. She maintained Alicia's vocabulary, her speech rhythms, her affective tells, her laugh.
- **Embodied autobiographical knowledge** sufficient to answer unrehearsed questions about Alicia's childhood, her stepfather, her sculptural practice, her past with Ben — including knowledge no Skrull intelligence dossier could plausibly contain in advance. The implication: she was either continuously updated by handlers (no evidence of dead-drops in the record) or, more likely, she improvised much of it and relied on the fact that no one was looking for the seams.
- **Sculptural skill.** Alicia is a working artist. "Alicia" continued to produce sculpture during the impersonation period — work that passed inside the gallery world. Lyja either possessed pre-existing artistic capability, learned it on assignment, or her shapeshifting extends to fine-motor neurological mimicry sufficient to replicate a trained craftsperson's hands. Any of these reads as exceptional.
- **Sexual and intimate impersonation.** Held against Ben Grimm and later Johnny Storm without breaking. This is not a skill polite intelligence files like to itemize, but the dossier is what it is: she successfully performed the most somatically intimate forms of attachment behavior with two men over years, including in conditions (sleep, orgasm, illness, grief) in which conscious role-performance is least defensible. The Skrull training that produced this is not on record. The cost of carrying it is on every page of §3.
- **Operational discipline.** Across years she never broke cover to send intelligence in a way the FF detected. Either her exfiltration was perfect or — and this is the alternative the file privileges — she stopped sending much intelligence at all, fairly early, because the role had begun to consume the operative.
