**Combat tradecraft, post-exposure:** When she fights openly she fights as an intelligence operative, not a brawler. She uses morphology for misdirection (false retreats, shape-swaps to draw fire, impersonation of allies to confuse enemy targeting), flares as interrupt-tools, and her knowledge of the FF's tactics — acquired during her embedded years — as a force multiplier when fighting alongside them. She is, functionally, the most dangerous person in any room to a Skrull strike team because she knows exactly how Skrull strike teams think.

---

### 6.4 Cognitive and Social Capabilities

**Theory of mind:** Extraordinary, by necessity. Sustained impersonation of a specific person in front of her intimates requires continuous, fine-grained modeling of how each observer expects the target to behave. She does this well enough that the FF — collectively one of the more perceptive groups in their world — missed her for years.

**Self-modeling:** Conspicuously poor, and this is not a paradox but a consequence. The cognitive bandwidth she devoted to modeling Alicia, Ben's expectations of Alicia, Sue's expectations of Alicia, and so on, was bandwidth not available for modeling herself. Operatives in this configuration commonly lose access to their own interiority; she did.

**Languages:** Skrull (native); English at native fluency; presumed working command of whatever languages the Alicia identity would have plausibly encountered. No evidence of polyglot range beyond mission requirements.

**Memory:** Operationally excellent. She retains detailed recollection of conversations and events from the impersonation period and references them with specificity in later appearances. There is no evidence of trauma-induced amnesia despite the conditions that would support it.

---

### 6.5 Growth, Decline, and Inflection Points

**Pre-mission (off-screen).** Trained operative; capability ceiling unknown but presumably standard infiltrator-grade.

**Embedded period (*FF* #265 ish – #357).** The shapeshifting discipline reached its lifetime peak. No other Skrull on record has held a single impersonation as long, as intimately, and against as perceptive an adversary group. This is her masterwork. It is also the period in which her self-modeling capability decayed.

**Post-exposure / reconditioning (*FF* #358 – #382).** Acquired the flare-blast augmentation. Combat lethality up. Identity coherence down. The Skrull rebuilders gave her more weapon and less self.

**Egg-deception period (*FF* #383 onward).** Capability turned inward in its most pathological form: the tradecraft she had honed for the Empire was deployed in service of a private grievance, against the man she most loved. The same skills that maintained "Alicia" maintained the false pregnancy. This is the only instance on record of her tradecraft serving neither mission nor conscience — and it is the diagnostic event of §3.

**Ally period (*FF* #393–#416, *Secret Invasion*, later cameos).** Capabilities stabilize at a new equilibrium. She no longer attempts sustained deep-cover impersonation; the work she does is short-form: brief mimicries, courier-runs of intelligence to the FF, combat support. The flares remain in the toolkit, used sparingly. Notably, she has not, in any post-redemption appearance, been depicted resuming the Alicia form. That capability is presumably intact and deliberately retired. The retirement is the tell.

**Late period (*Empyre* and after).** Operating openly as Skrull-presenting or hybrid-presenting in human spaces. The shapeshift, once her livelihood, is now used principally for *self-presentation* — choosing how visibly Skrull to appear in a given room — rather than for deception. This is the closest thing in the record to integration, and it is partial.

---

### 6.6 Hard Limits and Vulnerabilities

- **No documented resistance to standard Skrull species-vulnerabilities** as occasionally exploited in canon (hypnotic forced-reversion frequencies, certain energy signatures that disrupt morphology). She is no more hardened than her kin.
- **Mass-conservation ceiling** as noted above.
- **No flight, no super-strength beyond what a morphed musculature can simulate, no durability beyond Skrull baseline.** She is killable by ordinary means and has been "killed" once already.
- **Energy reserves for flare-projection appear finite and recover slowly.** She does not fight extended energy-projection battles.
- **Telepathic and high-end sensory detection** will defeat her impersonation work; she relies on the absence of such scans, not on resistance to them.
- **The deepest limit is not somatic.** She cannot impersonate a person toward whom she has unresolved feeling without the feeling leaking into the performance. The Alicia impersonation became compromised — internally, long before externally — at precisely the rate at which she began to care about Ben Grimm and then Johnny Storm as herself rather than as Alicia. Her power's failure mode is intimacy.

---

### 6.7 The Symptom-as-Signature Reading

Every capability in this file is also a wound, and the wounds map cleanly onto the powers.

The shapeshifting is the etiology of the dissociative disturbance in §4. A body that can be Alicia is a body in which Lyja is optional; a body in which Lyja is optional is a self in which Lyja is unconfirmed. The training that made her a perfect infiltrator was, mechanically, the same training that hollowed out the interior the infiltration was supposed to serve. The clinical literature on deep-cover decompensation describes exactly this trajectory in human operatives whose tradecraft did not include the literal cellular dissolution of the boundary between self and cover. She had the cellular dissolution as a starting point.

The flares are the Empire's after-the-fact verdict on what she had become. They were given to a woman who had failed at being a Skrull, by Skrulls who recognized that she could no longer be trusted as a face and would have to be reissued as a weapon. She turned the weapon on the issuers. The symbolism is not subtle and she lives inside it.

The tradecraft is the only province of the self in which her self-esteem is stable, and it is stable because it is the one capacity that does not require her to answer the question *who is doing this*. A spy does not need an integrated identity to run an operation. She has therefore organized large portions of her post-exposure life around tasks that resemble operations — couriering, infiltrating Skrull cells on the FF's behalf, running interference — because the operational frame is the frame in which she does not have to be anyone in particular, and in which competence substitutes for selfhood.

The single inability — the inability to impersonate cleanly in the presence of her own feeling — is the file's most hopeful datum. It is the precise location at which the manufactured operative failed and a person began. The power broke down exactly where the person grew in. Any prognosis worth the name in §4 rests on that breakdown: she is recoverable as a self to the degree that her shapeshifting continues to fail her around the people she loves, and she is endangered to the degree that she ever again succeeds at it.

— UATU, Analytical Stage, §6 closes.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 6: OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT

## Subject: LYJA

*Classification reminder: Skrull national, augmented field operative, defected; tradecraft assessment derived from a quarter-century behavioral record (1986 cover insertion forward) and cross-referenced against Skrull Imperial intelligence doctrine as inferred from comparable assets.*

---

## 6.1 Foundational Tradecraft Profile

Lyja is, by training and by demonstrated record, an **infiltration and impersonation specialist** of the highest grade the Skrull Empire fielded against Earth. Her operational lineage is not the brute substitution-and-kill model favored by Skrull line operatives (the "replace, exfiltrate the original, complete mission, withdraw" pattern visible in dozens of cheaper Skrull plays through the *Secret Invasion* archive). It is the **long-cover variant** — what a terrestrial service would call a *deep illegal*, an asset inserted into a target's intimate life and left there for years without active tasking, awaiting trigger events.

This distinction matters because it dictates everything else about how she works. A short-cover operative is trained to a script. A deep illegal is trained to a *life*. Lyja was given Alicia Masters's entire biography to absorb — childhood in Yancy Street, the relationship with the Puppet Master, the artistic vocabulary, the haptic vocabulary of a blind woman (the most operationally difficult element, requiring her to disable her own visual processing socially while retaining it tactically), Ben Grimm's preference structure down to dietary, sexual, and conversational micro-cues — and made to live it without performance lapses for years on end. Whatever else she is, she was the **best long-cover asset the Empire produced against the FF**, and her tradecraft reflects that pedigree throughout her later career, including the periods she works *against* her former employers.

### Core competencies inventory

- **Morphological impersonation** at biographical (not merely visual) fidelity, including voice, gait, mannerism, and the harder elements: idiolect, breathing rhythm, eye-movement patterns, sleep posture, lovemaking habit.
- **Behavioral mimicry of disability** (the Alicia blindness performance is the gold-standard datum here — sustained for years without exposure, including under intimate proximity to an investigative former-pilot turned adventurer).
- **Long-term cover maintenance** under conditions of total immersion with no handler contact for extended periods.
- **Counter-interrogation resistance** through dissociative identity-switching (she can offer truthful answers as one of her selves while the operational self remains uncompromised; this is both a tradecraft strength and the psychiatric problem in §3–4).
- **Augmented combat capability** (the retrofitted flare-blast power-set), of which her actual *use* is conservative — she does not lead with it; she leads with the impersonation, and the blasts are reserved for last-ditch defensive or distraction work.
- **Field bio-engineering literacy** sufficient to participate in the fabricated-pregnancy ruse, which required not just psychological staging but Skrull obstetric prop-work she presumably commissioned or self-administered.
- **Counter-Skrull operational knowledge** — she knows her own service's tells, code-protocols, recognition signs, fallback procedures, and emergency-exfil patterns, and after defection she weaponizes that knowledge selectively.

---

## 6.2 Decision-Making Process

Lyja's decision architecture, traced across the record, runs on three rails that frequently disagree with each other. Understanding the disagreement is the key to predicting her.

**Rail A — Operational rationality.** The trained-spy mind: threat assessment, asset/liability calculus, cover preservation, exit planning. This rail is fast, accurate, and almost always *available*. It is the only part of her cognition that operates with stable self-esteem (§5).

**Rail B — Attachment imperative.** The need-to-be-near-Johnny engine, with secondary pull toward Ben and the FF circle. This rail does not generate plans; it generates *vetoes* and *demands*. It vetoes any course of action that would mean leaving Earth permanently. It demands proximity even at operational cost.

**Rail C — Atonement ledger.** A quiet running tally of debts incurred — the original substitution of Alicia, the years of false intimacy with Ben, the egg deception, every Skrull operation she failed to warn the FF about in time. This rail biases her toward self-sacrificial options when a choice presents itself with roughly equal operational merit.

In practice: Rail A proposes, Rail B vetoes, Rail C breaks ties. The signature pathology of her decision-making is what happens when **Rail A and Rail B agree** on a course that Rail C cannot tolerate — she will execute the plan, but she will sabotage her own exit, manufacturing a circumstance in which she is captured, wounded, or believed-dead. The Paibok "death" is arguably the prototype: a confrontation she could have evaded, walked into.

**Decision latency:** very short for operational/tactical choices (sub-second; spy-trained); paradoxically long for personal/relational ones (days to years; she will sit on a needed conversation indefinitely). The asymmetry is diagnostic.

**Risk tolerance:** high for personal physical risk; near-zero for risks to the attachment objects; perversely high for *reputational/relational* risks where she will tolerate being seen as a monster (the egg ruse) if the alternative is being seen as nothing.

---

## 6.3 Methods & Tradecraft — The Working Repertoire

### Insertion & cover establishment

The Alicia substitution is the only complete-record case study, but its features are extractable as method:

1. **Pre-insertion biographical absorption** — Skrull cover-prep facilities (inferable from *FF* #357–358 deprogramming flashbacks) supply a target's full life-data; Lyja is observed to be exceptionally retentive of *micro-biographical* detail (the relational shorthand, the in-jokes, the unstated grievances within a family system).
2. **Original target exfiltration** — Alicia was held in Skrull custody; Lyja's role in the abduction is uncertain but she at minimum accepted the substitution as ethical, at that point in her arc.
3. **Soft insertion** under conditions favoring sensory and emotional ambiguity (Ben Grimm's depressive period and prolonged absences provided the cover-window; she was not required to mimic Alicia under maximal scrutiny on day one).
4. **Calibration phase** — incremental affect adjustment, watching for cover-failure signals; she demonstrates a clear capacity to *retreat* into more reserved, less-affect-rich behavior when uncertain, attributing it to mood, illness, or grief — the standard deep-cover mood-shield.
5. **Steady-state cover** — at which she remained for years, during which the operational drift that defines her file began: she went from *playing* Alicia to *being* a person who happened also to be a Skrull asset.

### Communication & handler contact

Across the cover period there is **no evidence of regular handler check-ins** — characteristic of a long-illegal protocol where check-ins are themselves the largest exposure vector. The pattern is: brief, asynchronous, terrain-disguised contacts, likely via Skrull operatives transiting Earth for unrelated business, with recognition-signs embedded in social interactions Alicia would plausibly have. Post-defection she retains the *capacity* for Skrull-protocol communication (recognition-signs, fall-back drops, emergency signals), which is why she has tactical value to terrestrial intelligence during *Secret Invasion* — she can read traffic her hosts cannot.

### Counter-surveillance / counter-detection

Her tells on this front, observable in the post-exposure period:

- She does not enter a room without locating exits; this is reflexive enough to be visible (a brief sweep at threshold, head-turn pattern characteristic of trained operatives).
- She seats herself with sightlines to entries and her back to a wall *unless* she is performing a cover identity that would not, in which case she suppresses the preference — but the suppression is itself visible as a momentary hesitation when selecting a chair.
- She varies routes; she does not return to the same place by the same path within a 48-hour window unless tactically required.
- She maintains a baseline awareness of who in any social setting could be a shapeshifter, evidenced by micro-pattern testing (asking small questions to which only the real person would know the answer, conducted so casually that targets do not register the test).
- She habitually scans for the specific tells of Skrull impersonation — pupil shape under stress, scent at close range, breathing rhythm during sleep — using her own knowledge of her people's failure modes.

### Combat doctrine

Combat is her **third-resort tool**, not first. Sequence in order of preference:

1. **De-escalation through cover** — be someone the opponent does not want to fight.
2. **Evasion via morphology** — become someone the opponent is not looking for, or something that cannot easily be tracked (smaller mass, infiltration form).
3. **Misdirection** — multiple impersonations, decoys, the manipulation of trust networks.
4. **Direct combat** — flare-blasts, hand-to-hand using Skrull strength baseline, only when prior options are foreclosed.

Her direct-combat style, where observed, is **economical and defensive** rather than offensive — short bursts of flare-blast at center mass intended to disable, then disengage. She does not pursue. She does not finish opponents who have stopped fighting. This is consistent across her record and is a behavioral marker of a trained agent rather than a soldier.

### The signature method: weaponized intimacy

Her single most distinctive tradecraft is the use of **established intimate relationship** as an operational instrument. The egg deception is the dispositive case but not the only one — across her record she repeatedly uses Johnny's emotional vulnerability to her as a vector, sometimes for legitimate purposes (warning, recruitment, extraction from a compromised situation) and at least once for what was effectively personal terrorism. This is the part of her tradecraft that operational doctrine cannot scrub clean. She knows how to use love as a lever because the Empire taught her, and because she learned that the lever worked on her too.

---

## 6.4 Resources, Finances, Infrastructure

A persistent puzzle in the file is **how the subject is materially supported**. The answer, derived from the behavioral record, is: minimally and improvisationally, by tradecraft.

**Finances:** No record of independent employment under any of her identities (the Alicia cover inherited an art career and a domestic-partner support structure; subsequent identities are episodic). Her financial pattern is consistent with an operative trained to live on **cached resources and opportunistic re-supply** — small amounts of currency moved through transient identities, brief cover-jobs taken for documentation rather than income, and substantial periods spent essentially as a guest/dependent in the Storm/Richards orbit when she is in residence. There is no evidence she has ever accumulated personal capital in any human currency. There is no evidence she values it.

**Documentation:** She can fabricate, or has access to fabricated, terrestrial identity documents through residual Skrull infrastructure (the same forgery pipelines that supplied her original Alicia documentation), and through whatever favors she can call in from Reed Richards's institutional connections when defected. Her identity portfolio at any given time likely contains 3–7 active human covers maintained at low intensity, plus the recognizable "Lyja" presentation she uses among the FF circle.

**Safehouses & residences:** No evidence of a permanent residence she calls her own. Her dwelling pattern is **rotational** — periods at the Baxter Building or its successors, periods aboard Skrull or terrestrial vessels in transit, periods in cover-residences (small apartments, taken short-term, abandoned without trace), and at least implied periods spent shape-altered and effectively *living as someone else's roommate or neighbor* for tradecraft cover. The absence of a home is both operational discipline and a symptom of the identity problem in §3.

**Equipment:** She travels light. The morphology *is* the toolkit — wardrobe, disguise, weapon, communication device (the flare-blasts double as signaling). She is not observed to carry significant terrestrial technology except when integrated into a specific cover. The only persistent personal-effect pattern is that she tends to retain a small number of **objects associated with the Storm/Grimm period** (a piece of jewelry, a fragment of clothing, a sketch from the Alicia identity that she is reluctant to destroy) — these are operationally indefensible and psychologically diagnostic; she will not throw them away.

**Networks (Skrull-side):** Largely burned. After exposure and Paibok, she has no reliable Skrull friends; she retains *knowledge* of Skrull intelligence structures, code-traffic patterns, and the identities of certain other Skrull operatives, which is the basis of her tactical value during invasion-era operations. Post-*Empyre* the picture is more complicated — the Skrull-Kree unification under Hulkling creates a notional polity in which she might in principle be a citizen in good standing, but she does not appear to have accepted that re-enfranchisement operationally; her behavior post-*Empyre* remains diasporic.

**Networks (human-side):** The FF and its extended circle (the Future Foundation, occasionally Avengers-adjacent contacts when an invasion is in play). She has *no* independent human friendships outside this circle on record — a profound social-poverty datum. She does not have a confidante. She does not have a clinician. She does not have a sponsor or a community. She has Johnny, sometimes, and Ben at a distance, and the children of the Richards family in a guarded, treasured way.

**Logistical signature:** Capable of appearing anywhere on Earth within hours when motivated; her morphology presumably allows infiltration of commercial transport without documentation friction. When she chooses to be untraceable, she is — there are extended gaps in the record (years at a stretch between the Hyperstorm aftermath and *Secret Invasion*) during which no terrestrial intelligence service can credibly claim to have known where she was.

---

## 6.5 Patterns of Action — Longitudinal Behavioral Periodicity

Reviewing the post-exposure record yields a recognizable **operational rhythm**:

**Phase 1 — Re-emergence.** Triggered by a crisis affecting Johnny or the FF, sometimes by a Skrull-side development she has detected. She arrives without warning, often in mid-action, often having already done the reconnaissance the team is about to attempt. Tradecraft tell: she rarely *announces* her arrival; she *appears* having already been present for some interval.

**Phase 2 — Operational integration.** She works alongside the team with maximal competence and minimal personal disclosure. Tradecraft tell: she will accept tactical leadership from Reed, Sue, or Johnny but will *not* accept psychological intimacy from anyone during this phase; she deflects personal questions with operational ones.

**Phase 3 — Attachment proximity.** Once the operational tempo slows, she drifts toward Johnny. This phase is the most volatile. She may attempt re-engagement; she may pre-emptively engineer distance; she may oscillate between both in a single conversation.

**Phase 4 — Withdrawal.** She disengages, usually without a clean goodbye, and disappears for periods of months to years. The withdrawal is presented operationally (a mission, a Skrull-side errand, a need to be elsewhere) but functions psychologically as a flight from the unresolvability of Phase 3.

This cycle has repeated, with variations, four or five times across the available record. It is **the most reliable predictor of her behavior**: any analyst attempting to project where she will be in 18 months should map current position on the cycle and extrapolate forward.

---

## 6.6 Signature Operational Tells

These are the granular markers an experienced surveillance team would log on her file — the involuntary signatures that survive every cover identity:

- **The chair-selection hesitation** noted above (§6.3).
- **A momentary pause before answering to a name** — any name, including "Lyja" — visible as a sub-second delay and a flicker of the gaze. She has too many names; she has to pick which self answers.
- **The Alicia-residue tells:** when distressed she occasionally lifts her hands as if to read a face or an object by touch, an Alicia mannerism that bled into her motor habits and which she has never fully suppressed. Under fatigue she may briefly soften her gaze in the unfocused way she trained for the blindness performance. These are the *most diagnostic* tells in her file and are almost impossible for her to eliminate because she does not consciously notice them.
- **Shapeshift "settling" microtremor:** after a morphological change held for an extended period, the surface of the assumed form will exhibit a faint micro-tremor for roughly 30–90 seconds while cellular configuration stabilizes. Visible only under close observation and good light.
- **Asymmetric concession in negotiation:** she will yield disproportionately to small requests, holding firm on large ones. Operational habit from cover work — small concessions buy social capital cheaply; large ones expose the cover.
- **Reluctance to eat in company** when in a non-Alicia/non-cover identity. Eating is intimate and Skrull metabolic preferences may differ from whatever form she is currently wearing; she manages the asymmetry by simply not eating where possible.
- **Sleep posture:** when she sleeps in proximity to others (rare), she sleeps in the posture of whatever identity she is currently wearing, not her own; her own posture is unknown to the record because she has not been observed sleeping as herself in any documented incident.
- **The "Alicia" word-stimulus response** (§5): pupillary dilation, breath catch, brief affective freeze, then over-controlled redirection. Repeatable under controlled conditions.
- **Refusal to be photographed in her Skrull baseline form.** Across the entire record there are perhaps a handful of images of her unaltered face; she manages this with such consistency that it is clearly deliberate. The Skrull baseline is the *one* identity she does not permit to be documented — possibly because it is the one she has the least claim to.
- **Operational disposal of personal effects with one exception** (§6.4): she abandons identities cleanly except for the small reliquary of Storm/Grimm-era objects she cannot let go. These are her tradecraft failure and her psychological signature.
- **A tendency to give warnings rather than orders** — she alerts, she advises, she pleads, but she very rarely commands, even when she has the tactical knowledge that would justify command. This is consistent with a self-concept that does not believe it has standing to direct others.
- **Use of the third person about her former selves:** "When I was Alicia…" rather than "When I was *pretending to be* Alicia." The grammar is the diagnosis.

---

## 6.7 Operational Summary

Lyja is, in the working sense, a **defected master-class long-cover operative with no remaining service**, no permanent residence, no independent income, no social network beyond the family she once deceived, and no integrated self from which to operate. That she remains, by any reasonable measure, **highly effective in the field** is a testament to the durability of her training and to the structural fact that operational tasks give her the only stable self-experience she has access to.

The practical handler/observer takeaways:

- She will work *with* the FF and against Skrull threats reliably, on her own initiative, without requiring tasking.
- She cannot be tasked *against* the FF or against Johnny Storm specifically under any circumstance; the attempt would either fail or destroy her.
- She is exploitable through her attachment objects in both directions (threat-to and indifference-from), but the exploitation has a moral cost the operating service should weigh.
- Her tradecraft is excellent and her self-knowledge is poor, which means she will execute brilliantly and choose badly. The choosing is where she needs help she has never asked for and would not accept if offered.
- The operational profile and the psychiatric profile are the **same document read in two directions**: every tradecraft strength is an identity wound, and every identity wound is a tradecraft strength. They cannot be separated, and any program of "rehabilitation" that treats them as separable will fail.

— *UATU, Analytical Stage; Section 6 of dossier closes. Cross-reference §3 (Psychological) and §5 (Personality) for integrated reading. Section 7 (Relationships — Granular Mapping) to follow.*


## Worldview & Operational Code

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 6
## WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE: SUBJECT "LYJA"

*Classification: derived from longitudinal behavioral record; inferential where direct testimony is absent; weighted toward action-evidence over stated belief, on the operating principle that the subject's stated beliefs are themselves a performance she half-believes.*

---

### 6.1 First Premises — The Metaphysics of the Performed Self

Lyja's lived cosmology begins from a single axiom, never spoken but everywhere demonstrated: **being is doing, and doing is being-watched-doing.** A Skrull infant raised into the impersonation discipline learns before language that the body is provisional, the face is a costume, and the *role* — the assignment, the cover, the brief — is the most stable thing in the room. Identity is therefore not an interior fact one possesses; it is an exterior fact one *performs sufficiently well that observers (including oneself) cannot detect the seam.*

From this premise descend several corollaries that govern her behavior across forty years of file activity:

- **Sincerity is a technique, not an essence.** One does not "be" sincere; one performs sincerity until the body's affective system is recruited into producing the corresponding feelings, at which point the performance becomes indistinguishable from the thing performed. Lyja knows this from the inside because it is what happened to her with Alicia Masters. Her marriage to Johnny Storm is the load-bearing evidence: she performed a wife so completely she became one, and the becoming was not a failure of tradecraft but the inevitable terminus of tradecraft taken to its limit.
- **The "real self," if it exists, is the residue left when all roles have been peeled away.** Lyja suspects this residue may not exist at all in her case — that she may be, structurally, a stack of impersonations with nothing underneath. She does not test the hypothesis directly because the testing might confirm it.
- **Bodies are wardrobe.** This is the Skrull cultural baseline, but Lyja holds it with an unusual ambivalence: she has lived in one face long enough to feel it as hers, and the experience has corrupted the orthodoxy. She no longer believes morphology is fully arbitrary. Some shapes leave marks.

### 6.2 The Reading of Other Persons

Operationally, Lyja reads people the way a forger reads signatures: stroke order, pressure points, the tell at the end of the loop. Her impersonation work required theory-of-mind at the asymptote — she had to model Alicia's interior so thoroughly she could produce Alicia's outputs *unprompted*, including in moments Alicia would never have been briefed on. The behavioral residue is a permanent diagnostic stance toward every person in the room:

- **First-pass scan:** posture, micro-tension at the jaw and hands, blink rate, the gap between the social smile and the eye crinkle that confirms it. Lyja is reading for cover, because she assumes everyone has one. (She is wrong about most humans and right about more Skrulls than the FF would like.)
- **Second-pass:** what does this person want from the room, and what are they pretending to want instead? She categorizes the gap. People with small gaps are safe; people with large gaps are interesting; people with no detectable gap are either saints or operators better than she is, and both warrant caution.
- **Third-pass, reserved for intimates:** what does this person *need* in a way they themselves have not articulated? This is the impersonator's gift turned to nurture. It is how she was a good Alicia. It is how she remains, when she chooses, a devastatingly attentive partner.

She does not extend this scan to herself. The diagnostic apparatus does not turn inward; turned inward, it would find the stack of selves and have to choose, and choice in that domain is foreclosed.

### 6.3 Conflict — Doctrine and Distaste

Lyja's conflict philosophy is **Skrull-trained but human-corrupted.** The training holds that conflict is won before contact through preparation, positioning, and the manipulation of the opponent's information environment; direct force is the admission that the prior phases failed. She still believes this. It is why her flare-blasts, despite being the augmentation her superiors invested in, are the part of her toolkit she uses with visible reluctance and only when subtler instruments have already been spent.

The corruption introduced by her years among humans — specifically among the Fantastic Four, who fight like a family argument that escalated — is an acquired distaste for conflict pursued past the point of necessity. She has watched Johnny burn things that did not need to burn, Ben break things that could have been talked down, Reed solve at the chalkboard what should have been solved at the dinner table. The result is a hybrid combatant doctrine:

1. **Avoid the engagement.** If the objective can be achieved by becoming someone the opposition does not perceive as a threat, do that.
2. **If engagement is forced, terminate it at the lowest energy state available.** A whispered word, a fabricated wound, a strategic disappearance.
3. **If force is required, apply it precisely and stop.** She does not pursue. She does not finish off. The post-combat behavior of a person who fought because she had to, not because she enjoyed it.
4. **The opponent worth defeating is the one who would have won.** Spectacle defeats are vulgar and informationally costly. Quiet defeats produce no martyrs.

She holds the Skrull warrior caste in moderate contempt for confusing item 3 with item 1. She holds Paibok in particular contempt, layered over fear, because he embodies the doctrine she rejected and because he killed her once already for rejecting it.

### 6.4 Control — Who Has It, How It Moves, How She Fights It

Lyja's theory of power is granular and unromantic. She does not believe in legitimacy; she believes in **leverage, inertia, and the willingness to use both.** The Skrull Empire taught her that authority is a costume worn by whoever is currently holding the relevant codes; the Fantastic Four taught her that authority can also be a thing a few people sustain by personal example, but that this version is fragile and depends on the example-givers continuing to show up.

Her operational beliefs about control:

- **Information asymmetry is the only real power.** Anyone who knows what you do not know controls the next move. This is why she protects intelligence assets with paranoia and why she gives information to allies only in the smallest functional units.
- **Institutions are weather.** They do not love you, they do not hate you, they will kill you if the front moves wrong. Plan accordingly. Carry shelter.
- **The handler-asset relationship is the basic political unit of the universe,** even between people who would call it by other names. She has been handled (Skrull command), she has handled (her targets), she has been handled by people who did not know they were doing it (Johnny, mostly, who never grasped how much of her behavior was responsive shaping to his moods), and she has tried to refuse handling and discovered she does not know who she is when no one is running her.
- **Self-control is the prerequisite for all other control.** She fails this one frequently and knows it. The egg deception is the file's standing rebuke.

### 6.5 Trust — Architecture and Failure Modes

Trust, in Lyja's working model, is **a graded credential, never a binary.** This is itself a deep-cover operative's habit of mind: the Skrull doctrine treats trust as a tactical issue (whom can I be in front of, in which face, while saying which things), and Lyja has never built a system for handling trust as an emotional fact. She has only the tactical version, which she now tries to use for emotional purposes with predictably poor fit.

Her credentialing structure, derived from observed access-granting behavior:

- **Tier 0 — Operational read-only.** Strangers, casual contacts, the general human and Skrull population. Lyja shows them a face and a backstory; both are disposable. She maintains no internal record of what she has told them.
- **Tier 1 — Functional collaborators.** Allies on a specific operation. She shows them competence and a thin layer of personality consistent with the operation's needs. She will protect them within the operation's frame and abandon them outside it without guilt.
- **Tier 2 — Persistent acquaintances.** The wider FF circle, certain Skrull defectors, working contacts she has dealt with across multiple incidents. She extends conditional candor and selective biographical disclosure. She does not let them see her destabilize.
- **Tier 3 — Witnesses.** People who have seen her decompensate and stayed in the room. The list is short. Ben Grimm is on it by accident of long marriage; Johnny Storm is on it by attrition. There may be no others.
- **Tier 4 — Reserved.** Empty. She has never granted this and may not be capable of granting it, because the credential it represents is *the right to know which of the selves is the real one*, and she would have to know that herself in order to confer it.

Trust failure, in her model, is not catastrophic; it is informational. When someone betrays her, she updates the tier and continues. The exception is Johnny, whose perceived withdrawals do not produce orderly downgrades but produce instead the high-stress collapse pattern documented in §5 — because Johnny was, in violation of her own doctrine, granted a credential she had no procedure for revoking.

### 6.6 Risk — Calibration, Asymmetry, and the Use of Her Own Body

Lyja's risk posture is the part of her operating system that is most clearly *trained* and least clearly her own. Skrull infiltration doctrine teaches a specific risk calculus: the operative is expensive (years of impersonation prep, surgical and behavioral conditioning, mission-specific cover construction) and therefore should not be wagered cheaply. Survival of the asset is itself a mission objective. This produces a conservative baseline.

Layered over this is the post-exposure Lyja, whose calculus has been deformed by the loss of any institutional principal whose interests she is preserving the asset *for*. The behavioral result is bimodal:

- **In service of a clear external objective** (warning the FF, extracting a target, infiltrating a Skrull cell on humanity's behalf), her risk-taking is professionally calibrated, often cautious, with strong attention to exit routes and contingency identities.
- **In service of an attachment objective** (proving devotion to Johnny, atoning toward Ben, demonstrating to herself that she is not the woman who staged the egg ruse), her risk-taking is wildly miscalibrated toward self-sacrifice. She accepts wound exchanges no professional would accept. She walks into rooms she would, on a working day, have surveilled for a week.

The asymmetry is diagnostic. The professional Lyja is preserving an asset for a principal; the personal Lyja is trying to spend the asset because she does not value it and because martyrdom would resolve the identity problem by closing it.

Her body, in this calculus, is **an instrument she does not fully count as hers.** This is the morphological substrate of the §3 self-concept finding. A shape she can change is a shape she cannot fully own; a shape she cannot fully own is one she can spend.

### 6.7 Loyalty — The Reorganization After the Empire Fell Out from Under Her

The Skrull Empire trained her to a loyalty model in which the state is primary, the unit is secondary, and the self is the instrument by which both are served. The state revealed itself, in her case, to be the entity that sent Paibok to kill her for the crime of having loved her cover too well. She has not had a coherent loyalty object at the species or political level since.

What she has constructed instead is **a loyalty of persons, not flags.** It is small, it is portable, it is the only loyalty structure she has found durable. The persons in it have been added one at a time, by the slow accumulation of evidence that they saw something in her and did not flinch:

- **Johnny Storm** — provisional permanent. The relationship is unresolved in every direction, but she has not removed him from the list across any documented stressor.
- **Ben Grimm** — a complicated entry. She owes him an apology she does not know how to deliver; she protects him at distance.
- **Alicia Masters, the real one** — an entry Lyja would never admit to. The woman whose life she stole has become, in Lyja's private cosmology, something between a victim she failed and a sister she never met. She has been observed (sparse data) avoiding Alicia in corridors when other choices were available.
- **Selected Skrull defectors** — a working caucus of the displaced, bound by shared estrangement rather than affection.

She does not extend loyalty to abstractions: not to "humanity," not to "the Skrull people," not to "the Earth," not to "the Empire," not to "the Foundation." When she fights for any of these, she is fighting for someone on the list above who has chosen to fight for the abstraction.

### 6.8 Truth and Deception — The Working Ethics of a Liar Who Wants to Stop

Lyja's relationship to truth is the most philosophically tortured region of her operating code, because lying is the only craft she has and she has come to suspect it is the thing destroying her.

Her working position, inferred:

- **Lies are tools and tools are morally inert; uses are not.** She does not feel guilt for deception per se. She feels guilt for *specific deceptions* in proportion to the damage they did to specific persons on her short list.
- **The unforgivable lie is the one that uses the target's love against them.** The egg ruse violated this rule, and her continued inability to fully forgive herself for it is the strongest available evidence that she holds it. The Alicia impersonation also violated it, retroactively, and she manages this knowledge by treating Alicia-the-cover as a different person from herself, a maneuver that is dissociatively expedient and morally evasive.
- **Truth-telling is a gift one owes the short list and almost no one else.** She does not believe in candor as a default; she believes in candor as a *credential*, granted along the same tier structure as trust.
- **The hardest truth to tell is the one about herself,** because she does not know which version of it is true, and the honesty would require admitting the unknowing, which would require admitting it to herself first.

### 6.9 Her Own Place in the World — The Inhabited Liminality

Lyja's most distinctive worldview commitment is the one she has made, by exhaustion and elimination, to **liminality as a permanent condition rather than a transitional one.** She has stopped trying to become Skrull again. She has stopped trying to become human. She has stopped trying to become "the integrated Lyja" the field's clinicians keep gesturing toward. What she has done instead, observably across the late-period record (Secret Invasion forward), is build a working life in the seam between categories and refuse to apologize for occupying it.

This is not enlightenment. It is *settlement.* The difference matters. An enlightened person inhabits liminality because they have transcended the need to belong. Lyja inhabits liminality because the alternatives have all failed and this is the configuration that produces the fewest acute crises per month. She is, in the language of refugees, *integrated by giving up on integration.*

The position has stable elements:
- She accepts the marginal status the FF extend her (helpful contact, not family member; trusted enough to call, not trusted enough to live in the building).
- She accepts the marginal status the Skrull diaspora extend her (one of us by birth, traitor by record, useful when useful).
- She has stopped pursuing the romantic resolution with Johnny that would force a categorical answer. She has not stopped *wanting* it; she has stopped pursuing it, which is a different and harder discipline.
- She has, in the same gesture, stopped pursuing the reverse — full estrangement, exile, a clean break that would also be a categorical answer. She lives in the not-answering.

### 6.10 The Code, Stated as She Would State It If Pressed

Reconstructed from the action record, in language she would recognize:

> *Be the role until the role is true. Watch the room before you enter it. Owe what you owe to the people who saw you and stayed; owe nothing to the flags they happen to stand under. Spend force last. Spend yourself before you spend a person on your list. Do not lie to the short list, and if you must, never with their love. Do not ask which of you is the real one; the question has no operational answer and the asking destabilizes the asset. Stay near the people who anchor you. Do not require them to name what you are to them. Do not name it yourself.*
>
> *And do not, under any pressure, do again what you did with the child that was not a child. That is the line. Past it, there is nothing you would recognize as yourself, and the small thing you are protecting by staying on this side of it is the only candidate you have left for a self at all.*

— UATU, Analytical Stage, §6 closes.


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP: SUBJECT DESIGNATE "LYJA"
## Section 6 — Moral & Ethical Framework

---

### 6.1 Preliminary Note on Method

The subject has never, in the recorded canon, delivered an extended articulation of her own ethics. There is no manifesto, no confessional monologue, no oath sworn aloud. What follows is therefore derived entirely from enacted behavior — what she has *done* under pressure, what she has refused to do when easier paths were available, and the asymmetries between her stated reasons and her observable choices. The framework reconstructed here is the framework she lives by; whether she could name it if asked is a separate question, and the evidence suggests she could not.

Her moral code is not the code of her upbringing. The Skrull Empire as represented across her operational history is a martial-imperial culture in which loyalty to the throne, success in mission, and species-supremacy form the spine of ethical instruction. Lyja's actual enacted code retains almost none of this. What replaced it was not adopted wholesale from her cover identity either — she is not "Alicia Masters with green skin." It is a third thing, assembled piecemeal under duress, and it is internally coherent in ways she has never had the chance to recognize.

---

### 6.2 The Operative Code (As Enacted)

**Tier One — Inviolable:**

1. *Do not let Johnny Storm die when you could have prevented it.* This is the closest thing in her record to an absolute. It has been honored under conditions of personal danger (multiple combat interventions during the Dreadface and Hyperstorm sequences), under conditions of disadvantage to her standing with the Skrull Empire (the *Secret Invasion* defection-by-warning), and under conditions where saving him cost her the chance to redeem herself in his eyes (she has repeatedly chosen his survival over his approval, which is a sharper test than survival over her own).

2. *Do not impersonate Alicia Masters again.* This prohibition is unspoken but observable. Despite possessing the technical capacity to resume that form at will — and despite the obvious operational advantages it would confer in many situations — she has not done so in any post-exposure appearance on record. The form is morally radioactive to her. To wear it again would be to confess that the original impersonation was a costume rather than a violation.

3. *Do not actively assist a Skrull operation against the Fantastic Four or Earth.* Passive non-cooperation would not satisfy this; she has on multiple occasions taken affirmative action to expose or sabotage such operations. The defection is enacted, not merely declared.

**Tier Two — Operative but Negotiable:**

4. *Tell the truth to Johnny when the alternative is letting him act on a false picture that could harm him.* Note the conditional. She is not committed to truthfulness as a virtue; she is committed to truthfulness as a protection. She has withheld information from him for what she construed as his benefit, and she has — once, catastrophically — lied to him as an act of attachment-aggression (the fabricated pregnancy). The rule is real but it is not categorical.

5. *Protect Skrull non-combatants when human conflict touches them.* Visible during the *Secret Invasion* and *Empyre* periods. The diaspora-loyalty is real but it activates only in specific configurations; she does not consider herself the protector of the Skrull Empire qua empire, only of Skrulls qua persons.

6. *Accept marginal status rather than force a confrontation that would require others to define her.* This is a moral commitment dressed as a temperamental preference. She believes — correctly, by the evidence — that demanding inclusion would damage the people whose inclusion she wants. So she withdraws. The ethic is one of *not imposing the cost of her unresolved self on others who did not create it.*

**Tier Three — Pragmatic / Situational:**

7. Deception in service of the protective mission is permitted. She remains, fundamentally, a spy; she lies fluently to enemies and to bystanders when the lie advances a protective end. The category "enemies" is now drawn around threats to Johnny, the FF, and her current chosen circle, rather than around the Skrull Empire's targets, but the deception faculty is intact and unrenounced.

8. Violence in defense of attached persons is permitted without hesitation. Violence in service of abstract causes is, by observation, refused or shirked.

9. Identity-performance in social contexts is permitted. She still passes, she still adapts, she still mirrors. She has not adopted a doctrine of radical authenticity; she has merely narrowed the range of impersonations she considers acceptable.

---

### 6.3 What She Will Not Do (Enacted Prohibitions)

The negative space of her code is more revealing than the positive. Across the record, the following actions are conspicuously absent despite repeated opportunity:

- **She will not kill a member of the Fantastic Four or their intimates.** Even at her most destabilized — during the period of the false-pregnancy revenge — she did not attempt lethal harm. The aggression was psychological, not physical, and it ran out of her quickly.
- **She will not deliver Skrull intelligence on the FF to Skrull command.** She possessed, for years, the most intimate possible knowledge of Reed Richards' household, security protocols, family vulnerabilities, and the children's routines. None of this has ever surfaced in a Skrull operation against the team. The most plausible explanation is that she never transmitted it — even during her active-cover period, the intelligence yield to her handlers appears to have been operationally thin. This is the earliest evidence of mission-creep into protection.
- **She will not impersonate a living person whose impersonation would deceive someone they love.** The Alicia prohibition generalizes. She will assume generic forms, tactical disguises, fabricated identities; she will not, on the record, wear another specific person's face into their family.
- **She will not denounce the Skrull Empire as a moral entity.** Her opposition is operational and particular. She does not preach against her own people. The reticence reads as residual loyalty but is more accurately understood as her refusal to take any totalizing stance about identity-categories — having been destroyed by one such totalization, she will not impose another.
- **She will not ask Johnny to choose her.** This is structurally the most important refusal in her file. She will save him, warn him, protect him, grieve him, and orbit him — but she will not force the question. The ethic here is partly self-protective (she could not survive the wrong answer) and partly genuinely other-regarding (she does not believe she has the standing to ask).

---

### 6.4 Justifications (Reconstructed)

Lyja does not articulate justifications in canon. The reconstructed justifications below are what her behavior implies she believes, even if she has never put it in these terms:

- *The original deception was wrong.* This is the bedrock conviction, and everything else is built on it. She does not euphemize the Alicia impersonation as "duty" or "orders" — when it is referenced, her affect is shame, not professional pride. The wrongness she perceives is not the impersonation per se but the *intimate use* of it: she stole emotional intimacy that was owed to another woman, and she gave physical intimacy under fraudulent identity. She treats both halves of this as injuries she inflicted, not as missions she completed.

- *Ben Grimm is the chief victim and is unreachable.* She has never, on record, attempted to make direct amends to Grimm. The avoidance is itself the ethics: she believes — correctly, probably — that her presence would worsen rather than relieve his wound. The unspoken rule is *the perpetrator owes the victim distance when proximity would be a second injury.*

- *Johnny's complicity does not reduce her culpability.* The Englehart marriage was technically consensual on his part, in that he believed he was marrying Alicia and proceeded freely on that belief. A lesser conscience would use this to redistribute blame. Lyja does not. She holds her culpability whole.

- *The egg deception was the second great wrong, and it was wholly hers.* Unlike the Alicia mission, which can be partially externalized as the Empire's design, the false pregnancy was unmistakably her own act, originating in her own woundedness, executed against her own better judgment. The post-deception behavioral record shows no attempt to justify it. She does not blame Johnny for provoking it; she does not blame Skrull conditioning for enabling it. The silence around this episode is the silence of a person who knows she has no defense and is not building one.

- *Atonement is owed but cannot be claimed.* She acts as if redemption is something one might be granted but never demanded. The protective courage is offered; she does not present it as a balance-sheet entry. This is unusual and morally serious. Most reformed-operative profiles in the broader case literature show some pattern of self-narration as redemption-in-progress; Lyja shows none.

---

### 6.5 Consistency — Where the Code Holds

The code, such as it is, holds with remarkable steadiness across two decades of in-story time. The protective priority around Johnny has never wavered. The Alicia-form prohibition has never been broken. The refusal to deliver intelligence to Skrull command has held even under captivity and reconditioning (the post-#358 period), which is operationally striking — reconditioned assets typically show drift back toward original handlers on stress, and she has not.

The consistency is most impressive in the *Secret Invasion* sequence. The Skrull-Earth conflict at that scale created precisely the forced-choice condition her psychology is least equipped to handle (§4: catastrophic stress = paralysis or martyrdom). She did not collapse into paralysis and she did not seek martyrdom. She chose the human side and made it operational. The choice was not aesthetically clean — she helped specific people, warned specific people, and did not denounce her species — but it was a *choice*, executed in the right direction, sustained over the arc. This is the strongest single piece of evidence that there is, in fact, a moral self under the dissociative weather, and that it has been quietly consolidating over time.

---

### 6.6 Fractures — Where the Code Breaks

**The egg deception (FF #383 ff.) is the dispositive fracture.** Every other apparent moral lapse in the record can be assimilated to operational necessity, indoctrination residue, or interpersonal confusion. This one cannot. She knowingly weaponized Johnny's grief and longing for a child, fabricated a pregnancy, and used the resulting emotional dependency to re-engineer his proximity. This was not done for the Empire. It was done for her. The cruelty was incidental to the goal (re-attachment) but it was foreseeable and she did not stop. The fracture this exposes is precise: *under abandonment cue, the protective code inverts and the attachment object becomes a target for manipulation rather than a recipient of care.* This is the borderline-trait signature noted in §4, expressed as a moral event.

**Secondary fracture — the maintenance of cover during the Alicia years.** It is easy in retrospect to characterize this period as pre-moral, a phase of indoctrinated automatism preceding her ethical awakening. The evidence does not fully support that framing. There are observable moments during the cover period (visible in the Englehart and DeFalco runs read against the post-#357 retrospective light) when she appears to choose intimacy beyond the mission brief — the marriage to Johnny being the largest such choice. If she had begun to feel by then, she had begun to be responsible by then. The cover-period conduct is therefore not morally inert; it includes years of sustained intimate fraud that she could, at various moments, have ended. She did not. The justification she would presumably offer — that breaking cover meant death at her own people's hands — is real but is the justification of a survivor, not the absolution of a moral agent.

**Tertiary fracture — selective truth with Johnny.** She has, in lower-stakes ways, withheld and shaded information across the post-defection period, sometimes for his benefit, sometimes for hers, and the line between the two is not always clean. This is the small-scale chronic version of the egg-deception pattern. It is also the place where her old professional faculty (spy-grade information control) refuses to retire.

---

### 6.7 Drift Over Time

The longitudinal trend is real and is in the favorable direction, though slow.

- **Cover period (FF #265–356, retrospective):** Operating ethics is mission-conformity with growing private exceptions; the exceptions are not yet legible to her as ethics.
- **Exposure and immediate aftermath (FF #357–382):** Moral life begins as panic and improvisation. No stable code. Loyalties in genuine flux.
- **Egg-deception period (FF #383–~390):** Acute moral failure under acute attachment crisis. This is the floor of her record.
- **Post-deception recovery (FF #393–416 era):** First sustained period of *enacted* ethics in the protective direction. Atonement-behavior begins. Marginal status is accepted rather than fought.
- **Liminal years (post-volume-3, scattered appearances):** The code stabilizes through repetition. She is becoming someone who reliably does certain things and reliably refuses others. Identity remains fractured but ethics begin to function as a partial substitute for identity — *what one does* fills in for *who one is.*
- **Secret Invasion (2008):** The code is tested at scale and holds.
- **Empyre and after (2020 →):** The Skrull-Kree unification offers, for the first time, a possible communal home that would not require her to repudiate either side of her divided self. She approaches it warily. The record does not yet show full integration; it shows tentative engagement consistent with her established refusal to demand inclusion.

The overall shape is: a person who began with no moral framework she had chosen, who passed through a profound failure, and who has been quietly assembling a small, particular, enacted ethics out of what she would and would not do, repeated across enough situations to begin to count as a self.

---

### 6.8 Comparative Note

There is no obvious analog in the meta-human case literature. The closest real-world structural parallel is the long-cover human-intelligence defector who marries into the target community, is exposed, and survives — a small population, but the pattern of post-exposure ethics in that population tends toward either total rejection of the original service (overcompensation, often performative) or partial-loyalty oscillation lifelong. Lyja's profile fits neither neatly. She does not perform repudiation and she does not oscillate in loyalty; she has settled, by enacted behavior, into a code organized around *particular persons* rather than *categories of persons*. This is the ethics of someone for whom categorical identity is the wound, and who has therefore had to build her morality entirely out of relationships to individuals.

It is, in its modest way, an unusual and dignified solution to an unusual injury. It is also fragile. Remove the few persons it is organized around and the code would have nothing to attach to. She would not become evil; she would become unmoored. This is the central operational finding for any party contemplating intervention in her circumstances: *her ethics is sustained by proximity to a very small number of people, and is not yet portable.*

— UATU, Analytical Stage, section closes.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP: SUBJECT DESIGNATE "LYJA"
## Section 6 — Communications & Linguistic Profile

---

### 6.1 Baseline Substrate: The Problem of a Native Tongue

The dossier must open with an unresolved foundational question: *what language does the subject think in?* Skrullos-standard is her natal tongue and the medium of her early training, yet the overwhelming majority of her documented adult life — by hours-on-record, by intimate exchanges, by the language in which she has loved, lied, and grieved — has been conducted in colloquial American English, specifically the New York/Lower Manhattan register absorbed first through Alicia Masters's social ecology (Yancy Street tradesmen, Greenwich Village gallery talk, the Baxter Building's hybrid technical-domestic patois) and later through prolonged exposure to the Storms.

The behavioral consequence: she has no neutral linguistic ground. When startled or in extremis she does **not** revert to Skrullos (a tell present in most cover-blown operatives); she reverts instead to *Alicia's cadences* — softer vowels, slightly elongated sibilants, a habit of beginning consoling statements with "Oh, honey—" or "Sweetheart, listen—" that is documented as early as her FF #265-era domestic dialogue and which surfaces involuntarily even decades later when she is comforting Johnny in *Secret Invasion*-era exchanges. The mother tongue, in any operationally meaningful sense, has been overwritten. This is itself diagnostic (§3 self-concept fracture): the deepest substrate of her speech is a stolen one.

### 6.2 Register Inventory

The subject commands at least five discrete registers, switched contextually with the fluency of a career impersonator:

**Register A — "Alicia-residual."** Soft volume, lower pitch than her natural Skrull range, sentences front-loaded with relational vocatives ("honey," "love," "sweetheart"), heavy use of tactile/sensory verbs ("feel," "hold," "stay"), and a deliberate slight slowness — the pacing of a sighted woman who once trained herself to speak as if to someone listening more than looking. Surfaces in intimate contexts and in moments of unguarded grief. She does not seem to know she does this.

**Register B — "Operational."** Clipped, declarative, low-affect, technically precise. Compound sentences pared to subject-verb-object. Tactical vocabulary deployed without elaboration ("perimeter," "exfil," "comms dark"). Pronoun economy: drops "I" where context allows ("Got it." "Moving." "Clear."). This is the register she uses with Sue Richards during crisis coordination and with Skrull defectors during *Secret Invasion*. Her most stable register, because it is the only one in which the identity question never arises — the operator-self has no name problem.

**Register C — "Skrull-formal."** Reserved for confrontations with her own species. Slightly archaic English syntax (suggesting she is translating in real time from Skrullos honorific structures), use of full titles ("Warlord," "Dard'van"), absence of contractions, and a chilly, slightly performative diction. The performativity is the tell: she is *playing* a Skrull more than being one, because the integrated Skrull-self atrophied during her cover years.

**Register D — "Confessional."** Rare. Reserved for Johnny, occasionally Sue, never Ben. Slower, longer pauses, frequent self-interruption, abandonment of complete sentences mid-thought ("I never — when I was her, I — you have to understand, I didn't know I was —"). Heavy in subjunctives ("if I could," "if you had ever"). The grammar of someone trying to assemble a self in the act of speaking.

**Register E — "Public-civilian."** A flat, slightly over-correct conversational English used with shopkeepers, bystanders, anyone outside the inner circle. Marginally too formal — the speech of someone who learned the language as an adult by watching it performed correctly and never quite shed the precision. Distinguishable from native NYC speech by the *absence* of regional shortcuts ("going to" rather than "gonna," "want to" rather than "wanna") in roughly 60–70% of recorded utterances, a frequency too high for a native speaker.

### 6.3 The Pronoun Tell

The single most reliable linguistic indicator of her internal state is **pronoun behavior around her own past**. Three distinct patterns recur:

1. **"When I was Alicia"** — used when she is composed, distanced, presenting herself as a recovered or recovering person. Indicates moderate stability; the "I" is doing integrative work.
2. **"When she was — when *I* was —"** — the self-correction tic. Indicates active dissociative slippage in the moment. She catches it, but the catch is audible. Frequency increases under stress and in Johnny's presence.
3. **"Alicia would have —"** — third-person reference to her cover identity. Almost always appears when she is contemplating an action she cannot perform as herself (a tenderness, a domestic gesture). Most dangerous indicator: signals that the cover identity is being treated as a separate ego-state with its own agency. Documented in the post-egg-deception period and in scattered Hickman-era cameos.

A complete file note: the pronoun "we" virtually never appears in her speech in reference to either Skrulls or the FF. She does not belong to a first-person plural. This is among the loneliest things about her recorded vocabulary.

### 6.4 Verbal Tics and Micro-Patterns

- **The half-laugh.** A short, voiceless exhalation that punctuates her own painful admissions, transcribed in scripts as "heh" or "ha." Functions as a self-deprecating buffer; appears almost exclusively in Register D.
- **The trailing "—"**. Her dialogue is unusually heavy in em-dashes and ellipses (a stylistic choice the writers have maintained with surprising consistency from DeFalco through Slott). She begins thoughts and abandons them. Roughly one in four of her sustained dialogue panels in the post-revelation era ends without terminal punctuation.
- **Negation-before-assertion.** "I don't — I never meant —" "I'm not — I wasn't —". She prefers to define what she is not before risking what she is. A diagnostic linguistic shape for fractured self-concept.
- **The name "Johnny."** Said with measurably higher frequency than functional discourse requires. She uses the proper noun where a pronoun would suffice; she addresses him by name mid-sentence ("I know, Johnny, I know"). This is a verbal anchoring behavior — the name as tether.
- **Absence of the name "Ben."** When she refers to Grimm she most often uses circumlocutions ("him," "your friend," "the one I —"). The name itself is largely avoided. Avoidance is the form her guilt takes in syntax.
- **The phrase "I had to."** Recurring justificatory tic. Appears in mission-explanation contexts and in self-exculpation alike, with no apparent distinction between true operational necessity and rationalization. A handler should note this phrase as a flag for self-deception in progress.
- **"You don't understand."** Frequent. Almost always accurate — interlocutors generally don't — but functions as a conversational lock that ends discussion rather than opens it.

### 6.5 Diction and Lexical Footprint

Lyja's working vocabulary is **bimodal**: a domestic-emotive register inherited from the Alicia immersion (heavy in sensory and relational nouns — *home*, *quiet*, *warm*, *stay*, *hold*) and a martial-operational register inherited from Skrull training (*target*, *protocol*, *extraction*, *asset*, *cover*). The middle range — the casual conversational vocabulary of a person with hobbies, opinions, idle preferences — is conspicuously thin. She does not have small talk. When small talk is socially required, she imitates Alicia's; when Alicia's repertoire is exhausted, she falls silent.

Notable absences from her lexicon: 
- **Skrull cultural idioms in English translation.** She does not bring proverbs, oaths, or folk references from her own culture into her English speech, in marked contrast to most other defected-Skrull characters on record. She has cut that root.
- **Religious or cosmological vocabulary.** No invocations of Skrull deities, no oaths "by the Throne," nothing. Either she was never inducted into that layer of her culture or she has actively suppressed it.
- **Future-tense planning at the personal scale.** She speaks fluently in operational futures ("we'll hit the perimeter at —") but rarely in personal ones ("next year I'll —"). She does not project a personal future in language. This is among the most clinically significant absences in the file.

### 6.6 Rhetoric

In persuasion she relies on three modes, in order of frequency:

1. **Demonstrated action over argument.** Her preferred rhetorical move is to *do* the protective or sacrificial thing and let the action speak. She is uncomfortable making her case verbally and tends to undersell her own loyalty in words, overcompensating in deed. Operationally this means she is more credible in the field than in the debrief.
2. **Appeal to shared past.** When she does argue verbally, her structure is almost invariably retrospective ("you remember when —" "after everything we —"). She does not argue from principle; she argues from accumulated intimacy. Notable that this rhetorical mode is unavailable to her with Skrulls, since her shared past with them is the past she has betrayed.
3. **Appeal to her own unreliability.** A peculiar inverse-rhetoric: she frequently cedes the moral high ground preemptively ("I know you have no reason to believe me, but —"). This is partly genuine and partly tactical — disarming the interlocutor's distrust by naming it first. Effective; her credibility with Sue Richards specifically has been rebuilt largely through this device.

She does **not** use threat-rhetoric. In the full record there is no instance of her threatening an interlocutor in words; when she means harm she simply causes it. The absence of verbal threat in a being with energy-flare capability is itself a tell: her violence is decided privately and executed without negotiation.

### 6.7 How She Communicates Love

Love-language inventory, in descending order of frequency:

- **Practical service.** Bringing food, repairing damage, providing intelligence unrequested. She loves by *handling things*. The Alicia residue is heavy here.
- **Physical proximity without speech.** Sitting nearby. The hand on the shoulder. She is most fluent in love when she is not required to translate it into words she does not trust.
- **The name, spoken.** As noted in §6.4, repeated naming functions as her most consistent verbal love-marker.
- **Self-deprecating concession.** "You're right. I should have —" She loves by losing arguments she could win.
- **Direct verbal declaration: rare and high-cost.** When she says "I love you" — a small number of documented instances, almost all to Johnny, most clustered around moments of expected separation or apparent-death — it arrives without ornament, often as a flat, slightly resigned statement rather than an effusion. She does not gild it because she does not trust her own gilding.

What she does **not** do, and the absence is significant: she does not flirt. The seductive register is entirely absent from her post-exposure speech, despite being morphologically and tonally available to her. This is interpreted as a deliberate self-prohibition — flirtation is the operational mode of seduction-cover work, and she will not redeploy it in earnest because the contamination would be unbearable.

### 6.8 How She Communicates Threat

As noted: rarely in words. When she does, the verbal threat takes the form of **flat, declarative warning** — never escalating, never repeating. "Step away from him." "Don't." Single clauses, no modifiers, no profanity. The absence of escalation language is itself the threat: she has skipped the negotiation phase entirely. Skrull opponents in particular receive a marginally different variant — sentences in the Skrull-formal register that read as ritual challenge ("I will not let you —"), suggesting some buried training in martial declamation.

She does not engage in trash-talk, taunting, or rhetorical sadism. The vocabulary of dominance is unused.

### 6.9 How She Communicates Grief

This is the most diagnostically rich domain.

Her grief-speech in the immediate aftermath of loss (Johnny's rejection, the Paibok attack, the egg revelation collapse) follows a consistent shape:

1. **Initial verbal arrest.** A documented several-panel pattern of attempting to speak and failing. Open mouth, no utterance, written in scripts as ellipsis-only dialogue balloons.
2. **Repetition of a single word or phrase**, usually the interlocutor's name or a flat denial ("No. No. Johnny, no.").
3. **Self-blame in fragmentary syntax.** "I did this. I — I did this."
4. **Withdrawal of speech entirely.** She goes silent and physically leaves. The exit is itself her closing statement.

Notably absent in her grief: blame of others (even when warranted), elaborated narrative of the loss, request for comfort. She does not ask to be held. She does not say "I need you." The grief is conducted as a solo discipline because she does not believe the comfort, if offered, would be aimed at the right person.

### 6.10 Deflection Language and Evasions

Catalogued deflection patterns, by frequency:

- **Topic-pivot via operational urgency.** "We can talk about that later — right now —". The mission is always available as an exit from interiority.
- **Apology as termination.** "I'm sorry" deployed not as opening but as closing — a way to end a conversation by accepting blame so the interrogation has nowhere to go.
- **Literalization of metaphor.** When pressed on emotional questions she sometimes retreats into literal-mindedness ("What do you mean *home* — I have no home"). This is partly cultural-linguistic (Skrullos may be a more literal idiom; insufficient data) and partly a defensive narrowing of the conversation.
- **The unfinished sentence as full stop.** Allowing the trailing "—" to stand as her entire answer, daring the interlocutor to complete it for her.
- **Reflective question.** Returning a question with a question, usually softer ("Why are you asking me that?"). Spy-craft origin, deployed personally.

She does **not** lie under direct questioning by intimates anymore. The cost of the original deception was too high; her post-exposure record shows a pronounced, almost compulsive truth-telling when pressed by Johnny, Sue, or the assembled FF, even when truth is operationally suboptimal. She will *evade*, she will *not answer*, she will *leave* — but she has not been recorded in a substantive lie to those four faces since approximately the conclusion of the Hyperstorm arc. This is one of her best prognostic indicators.

### 6.11 Tells: Linguistic Indicators of Internal State

For handler/analytical use, in order of reliability:

1. **Pronoun slippage on the past self** (§6.3) — the single highest-confidence indicator of acute dissociative stress.
2. **Code-switch into Register A (Alicia-residual) under combat or crisis** — indicates she is regressing toward the most overlearned attachment-script available to her. Often accompanies protective overfunctioning toward Johnny.
3. **Sudden adoption of Register C (Skrull-formal)** in mixed company — indicates she is bracing for or performing repudiation of her own species, often a precursor to violence against other Skrulls.
4. **Disappearance of contractions** — under intense self-monitoring, contraction rate drops to near zero. A reliable indicator she is choosing each word, which means she does not trust the conversation.
5. **Increased name-frequency for the addressee** — anchoring behavior, indicates escalating attachment-anxiety in the exchange.
6. **Use of "Alicia" as third-person subject** — red flag (§6.3 item 3), indicates the dissociative ego-state is being foregrounded; intervention threshold.
7. **Complete shift into silence in mid-conversation** — not refusal but inability; she has lost access to the register the moment requires. Most often observed in confrontations involving Ben Grimm or reproductive themes.
8. **Use of "I had to"** — flag for self-deception in progress (§6.4).
9. **The half-laugh** (§6.4) preceding an admission — marker of an attempt at self-truth that is costing her; the admission that follows is usually accurate.

### 6.12 Cross-Era Stability

A note for the longitudinal record: across thirty-plus years of published appearances and multiple authorial hands, the linguistic profile has remained startlingly consistent. The pronoun problem, the name-anchoring, the em-dash syntax, the avoidance of "Ben," the Alicia-residue in tender moments, and the operational-register cleanness all persist from DeFalco through Englehart-retroactive readings, through the *Secret Invasion* dialogue, through Hickman's sparse use, through *Empyre* and Slott. This is not necessarily authorial intent maintained; it is just as likely the structural inevitability of the character — given who she was made to be, there is no other way for her to speak.

She has not, in three decades of record, developed a new register. The vocabulary of *Lyja-as-herself*, the sixth register that would integrate the others, has never been observed in the file. Its absence is the file's central linguistic finding.

— UATU, Analytical Stage, communications subsection closes.


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

## Forecasting framework

The following are conditional predictions: *given* a stimulus or situation the canon never staged, *expect* the behavior derived from the established personality architecture (§3–§5). Each is annotated with the underlying mechanism, the confidence interval (H/M/L), and — where relevant — the observable tell that would confirm the prediction in field observation.
